Title: The Voter Identification Regulations 2022
Date: 2024-11-19
Description: These Regulations make provision related to the requirement for voters to present photographic identification when voting at polling stations at UK Parliamentary elections in Great Britain. These Regulations also create a similar requirement for persons voting at polling stations at Police and Crime Commissioner elections in England and Wales, and local government elections and referendums in England, and a similar requirement for persons signing a recall petition held in Great Britain under the Recall of MPs Act 2015 (c. 25) when signing the petition at a petition signing place.
Publisher: Statute Law Database
Identifier: http://www.legislation.gov.uk/uksi/2022/1382

## The Voter Identification Regulations 2022

    Council Tax, England       Local Government, England       Police, England
And Wales       Representation Of The People       Town And Country Planning,
England

  Made   22nd December 2022

  Coming into force in accordance with regulation 1

      The Secretary of State makes the following Regulations in exercise of
the powers conferred by the provisions specified in Schedule 1 to these
Regulations.       The Secretary of State has consulted—     a     the
Electoral Commission, in accordance with section 53(5)(a) of the
Representation of the People Act 1983 , paragraph 16(5) of Schedule 4B to the
Town and Country Planning Act 1990 , section 52ZQ(6) of the Local Government
Finance Act 1992 , section 9HE(4) of the Local Government Act 2000 , section
7(1) and (2)(e), (hc) and (k) of the Political Parties, Elections and
Referendums Act 2000 , and paragraph 12(4) of Schedule 5B to the Local
Democracy, Economic Development and Construction Act 2009 ,         b     the
Information Commissioner and such other persons as the Secretary of State
considered appropriate, in accordance with section 53(5)(b) and (c) of the
Representation of the People Act 1983,         c     the Scottish Ministers,
in accordance with section 15(5C) of the Representation of the People Act 1985
, and         d     the Welsh Ministers, in accordance with section 15(5D) of
the Representation of the People Act 1985 .               A draft of these
Regulations has been laid before, and approved by resolution of, each House of
Parliament in accordance with section 201(2) of the Representation of the
People Act 1983 , section 333(3A) of the Town and Country Planning Act 1990 ,
section 52ZQ(7) of the Local Government Finance Act 1992, section 105(6) of
the Local Government Act 2000 , section 117(2) of the Local Democracy,
Economic Development and Construction Act 2009 , section 154(2)(b) of the
Police Reform and Social Responsibility Act 2011  and section 21(6) of the
Recall of MPs Act 2015 .

### Introduction

#### Citation, commencement and saving

1

1.1

These Regulations may be cited as the Voter Identification Regulations 2022.

1.2

This Part and regulation  14(6)  come into force on the 22nd day after the day
on which these Regulations are made.

1.3

Subject to paragraphs (4) and (5), the remainder of these Regulations come
into force on the 25th day after the day on which these Regulations are made.

1.4

Regulations  38(2) ,  39(2)  and  41  come into force on the first day on
which a provision of Part 3 of the Domestic Abuse Act 2021  comes into force,
including where that provision is brought into force for a specified purpose
or in relation to a specified area under section 90 of that Act.

1.5

Regulation  40(2)  and (3) comes into force at the end of 28th February 2023.

1.6

The provisions listed in paragraph  (7)  do not apply in relation to—

1.6.a

a parliamentary general election to which paragraph 18 of Schedule 1 to the
Elections Act 2022  does not apply;

1.6.b

a relevant election, petition or referendum, other than a parliamentary
general election, in respect of which the qualifying date is on or before 3rd
May 2023.

1.7

The provisions are—

1.7.a

Parts 6 to 8;

1.7.b

in Part 9, regulations  38(4)  to (8) and (11) and  39(4)  to (8) and (11);

1.7.c

Part 10.

1.8

In paragraph  (6)(b) , “qualifying date”—

1.8.a

where the relevant election, petition or referendum is a recall petition,
means the beginning date of the signing period as specified in the public
notice of petition given under regulation 14 of the 2016 Regulations ;

1.8.b

otherwise, means the date of poll as specified in the notice of election or
referendum published in accordance with rule 5 of the elections rules.

#### Extent

2

2.1

This Part extends to England and Wales, Scotland and Northern Ireland.

2.2

Parts 2 to 7 extend to England and Wales and Scotland, and the following also
extend to Northern Ireland—

2.2.a

regulation  23 ;

2.2.b

in regulation  24 , paragraph (2) and, so far as it applies to that paragraph,
paragraph (3).

2.3

Any amendment made by Parts 8 to 10 has the same extent as the provision
amended, except the amendments made by regulations  70  to  75 ,  77  to  82 ,
86 ,  88 ,  90 ,  91(a)  and  92 , which extend to England and Wales and
Scotland only.

#### Interpretation

3

3.1

In these Regulations—

“ the 1983 Act ” means the Representation of the People Act 1983; “ the 2016
Regulations ” means the Recall of MPs Act 2015 (Recall Petition) Regulations
2016; “ anonymous elector’s document ” means that document as designed by the
Electoral Commission in accordance with regulation  15(1)(a)  or (d) or (4) ;
“ combined authority mayoral election ” means an election for the return of a
mayor as provided for in an order made under Schedule 5B to the Local
Democracy, Economic Development and Construction Act 2009;   “ combined county
authority mayoral election ” means an election for the mayor as provided for
in regulations made under Schedule 2 of the Levelling-up and Regeneration Act
2023;   “ digital service ” means the Individual Electoral Registration
Digital Service, which is the digital service provided by the Secretary of
State for the purpose (amongst other purposes) of processing online
applications for electoral identity documents under section 13BD of the 1983
Act  and for verifying information in accordance with regulation  6 ; “
electoral identity document ” means that document as designed by the Electoral
Commission in accordance with regulation  15(1)(b)  or (d) or (4) ; “ identity
document application ” means— an application for an electoral identity
document under section 13BD of the 1983 Act, or an application for an
anonymous elector’s document under section 13BE of the 1983 Act ; “ issued
document record entry ” means an entry in the record kept in accordance with
regulation  20  in respect of an anonymous elector’s document, or an electoral
identity document, issued by a registration officer; “ local authority mayoral
election ” means an election in England for the return of an elected mayor as
defined by section 9H(1) of the Local Government Act 2000 ; “ PCC election ”
means an election of a police and crime commissioner under Chapter 6 of Part 1
of the Police Reform and Social Responsibility Act 2011 ; “ petition signing
place ” has the meaning given in regulation 3(1) of 2016 Regulations; “ recall
petition ” has the meaning given by section 1 of the Recall of MPs Act 2015; “
registration officer ” means an electoral registration officer; “ signing
period ” has the meaning given by section 9(2) of the Recall of MPs Act 2015;
“ signing sheet ” has the meaning given by regulation 10 of the 2016
Regulations; “ specified document ” has the meaning given by rule 37(1H) and
(1K) of the elections rules; “ temporary electoral identity document ” means
an electoral identity document that has a temporary validity, as designed by
the Electoral Commission in accordance with regulation  15(1)(c)  or (d) or
(4).

3.2

In these Regulations other than in regulations  14(7)  and  20(7) , “ bank
holiday ” means—

3.2.a

subject to paragraph (3), in relation to a parliamentary general election, a
day which is a bank holiday under the Banking and Financial Dealings Act 1971
in any part of the United Kingdom, and

3.2.b

in relation to any other relevant election, petition or referendum—

3.2.b.i

where the relevant election, petition or referendum is held in an area in
England or Wales, a day which is a bank holiday under that Act in England and
Wales;

3.2.b.ii

where the relevant election, petition or referendum is held in an area in
Scotland, a day which is a bank holiday under that Act in Scotland.

3.3

Where at a parliamentary general election any proceedings are commenced afresh
by reason of a candidate’s death, the meaning of “bank holiday” in paragraph
(2)(b) applies in relation to that election rather than the meaning in
paragraph (2)(a).

3.4

In these Regulations, “ relevant election, petition or referendum ” means an
election, petition or referendum listed in the first column of the following
table; and the “relevant officer” for such an election, petition or referendum
means the officer listed in the corresponding entry in the second column of
that table—

Election, petition or referendum Relevant officer A parliamentary election in
England, Wales or Scotland The returning officer or (in England and Wales) an
acting returning officer A recall petition in England, Wales or Scotland The
petition officer within the meaning of section 6 of the Recall of MPs Act 2015
A PCC election The police area returning officer within the meaning of article
2(1) of the Police and Crime Commissioner Elections Order 2012    A local
government election in England The returning officer A local authority mayoral
election The returning officer within the meaning of regulation 2 of the Local
Authorities (Mayoral Elections) (England and Wales) Regulations 2007    A
combined authority mayoral election The   combined authority  returning
officer within the meaning of article 2 of the Combined Authorities (Mayoral
Elections) Order 2017      A combined county authority mayoral election  The
combined county authority returning officer within the meaning of article 2 of
the Combined Authorities (Mayoral Elections) Order 2017 A referendum under
Part 1A of the Local Government Act 2000    The counting officer within the
meaning of regulation 9 of the Local Authorities (Conduct of Referendums)
(England) Regulations 2012    A referendum under Chapter 4ZA of Part 1 of the
Local Government Finance Act 1992    The counting officer within the meaning
of regulation 15 of the Local Authorities (Conduct of Referendums) (Council
Tax Increases) (England) Regulations 2012    A referendum under Schedule 4B to
the Town and Country Planning Act 1990 The counting officer within the meaning
of regulation 9 of the Neighbourhood Planning (Referendums) Regulations 2012

3.5

Except in Part 7, a reference in these Regulations to a numbered rule in the
elections rules is to be read as a reference to—

3.5.a

in the case of a parliamentary election, the rule of that number in the
parliamentary election rules in Schedule 1 to the 1983 Act ,

3.5.b

in the case of a recall petition, the corresponding regulation in the
regulations made under section 18(1) of the Recall of MPs Act 2015, or

3.5.c

the corresponding rule in the rules made under—

3.5.c.i

in the case of a PCC election, section 58(1)(a) of the Police Reform and
Social Responsibility Act 2011 ,

3.5.c.ii

in the case of a local government election in England, section 36 of the 1983
Act ,

3.5.c.iii

in the case of a local authority mayoral election, section 9HE(1)(a) of the
Local Government Act 2000,

3.5.c.iv

in the case of a combined authority mayoral election, paragraph 12(1)(a) of
Schedule 5B to the Local Democracy, Economic Development and Construction Act
2009,

3.5.c.iva

in the case of a combined county authority mayoral election, paragraph
12(1)(a) of Schedule 2 to the Regeneration and Levelling-up Act 2023,

3.5.c.v

in the case of a referendum under Part 1A of the Local Government Act 2000,
section 9MG(2) or (3) of that Act ,

3.5.c.vi

in the case of a referendum under Chapter 4ZA of Part 1 of the Local
Government Finance Act 1992, section 52ZQ(1) or (2) of that Act, or

3.5.c.vii

in the case of a referendum under Schedule 4B to the Town and Country Planning
Act 1990, paragraph 16(1) of that Schedule.

### Applications for electoral identity or anonymous elector’s documents

#### Identity document applications: general

4

4.1

An identity document application must be in writing, and must state—

4.1.a

the applicant’s full name;

4.1.b

the address in respect of which the applicant is registered, or has applied to
be registered, on the register of parliamentary electors or local government
electors;

4.1.c

where the applicant is or has applied to be registered in pursuance of—

4.1.c.i

a service declaration, the applicant’s present address, correspondence address
or British Forces Post Office Number;

4.1.c.ii

an overseas elector’s declaration, the applicant’s present address;

4.1.d

the applicant’s date of birth or, if they are not able to provide that
information, the reason why they are not able to do so and a statement as to
whether the applicant is under 18 years old;

4.1.e

the applicant’s national insurance number or, if they are not able to provide
that information, the reason why they are not able to do so;

4.1.f

an indication as to whether, if the identity document application is granted,
the applicant considers that it is necessary for the applicant to collect the
document in person instead of the document being delivered to the relevant
delivery address, and if so the reason why the applicant considers that
collection is necessary;

4.1.g

for an identity document application under section 13BE of the 1983 Act, the
fact that the applicant has applied or is applying to have an anonymous entry
on the register;

4.1.h

an indication as to whether, if the identity document application is granted,
the applicant requires a Braille, easy read or large print explanation of the
anonymous elector’s document or the electoral identity document issued;

4.1.i

a declaration by the applicant that the information provided in the
application is true;

4.1.j

the date of the application.

4.2

Where an applicant makes an identity document application by virtue of section
13BD(1)(b)(ii) or section 13BE(1)(b)(ii) of the 1983 Act (applicants
registered in Wales who will be entitled to vote in police and crime
commissioner elections upon attaining the age of 18)—

4.2.a

if the applicant is not able to provide their date of birth, the statement
referred to in paragraph  (1)(d)  must indicate whether the applicant is—

4.2.a.i

under the age of 16, or

4.2.a.ii

aged 16 or 17;

4.2.b

paragraph  (1)(e)  does not apply where the applicant is under the age of 16.

4.3

An identity document application must also include—

4.3.a

a photograph of the applicant which meets the requirements set out in Schedule
2, and

4.3.b

where, in accordance with paragraph 3(2) of that Schedule, the applicant is
unable to provide a photograph that complies with paragraph 3(1)(d) or (e) of
that Schedule, the reason why they are not able to do so.

4.4

An identity document application may (but need not) include the applicant’s
email address and telephone number.

4.5

Where the applicant is not able to provide a national insurance number, the
applicant may provide as part of an identity document application a copy of
any of the documents listed in—

4.5.a

where the applicant has applied or is applying to have an anonymous entry on
the register, regulation  7(3)  to (5);

4.5.b

otherwise, regulation  7(4)  or (5).

4.6

A registration officer may authorise an applicant to provide anything which
must or may be included in or with, or which may be provided as part of, an
identity document application in accordance with this regulation to the
registration officer in person and, where the officer does so, the
registration officer must transfer anything provided by the applicant into an
application in writing.

4.7

In paragraph  (1)(f) , “ relevant delivery address ” means—

4.7.a

where paragraph  (1)(c)  applies, the address provided in accordance with that
paragraph;

4.7.b

where paragraph  (1)(c)  does not apply, the address provided in accordance
with paragraph  (1)(b) .

#### Identity document applications made through the digital service

5

5.1

This regulation applies where, by virtue of arrangements made by the Secretary
of State, an identity document application for an electoral identity document
under section 13BD of the 1983 Act may be made through the digital service.

5.2

The Secretary of State may complete an identity document application in part
for an applicant using information provided by the applicant as part of an
application, or partially completed application, under section 10ZC or 10ZD of
the 1983 Act  for registration in, or alteration of, a register of electors
made through or completed using the digital service.

5.3

The Secretary of State must send to the appropriate registration officer any
identity document application the Secretary of State receives  , subject to
paragraph (4),   together with a reference number unique to that application.

5.4

Where an application made through the digital service includes the applicant’s
national insurance number the Secretary of State—

5.4.a

may send the registration officer that application without the national
insurance number, and

5.4.b

where the Secretary of State does so, must indicate to the registration
officer that a national insurance number was included when the application was
made by the applicant.

#### Verification of information provided in an identity document application

6

6.1

On receipt of an identity document application made otherwise than through the
digital service, a registration officer must disclose the applicant’s name,
relevant address, date of birth and national insurance number (“the first
stage information”) to the Secretary of State for   Housing, Communities and
Local Government   in such format and through such an infrastructure system as
the Secretary of State for   Housing, Communities and Local Government   may
have notified to the registration officer in writing.

6.2

Following receipt of the first stage information from the registration officer
or (in the case of an application made through, or partially completed using,
the digital service) from an applicant, the Secretary of State for   Housing,
Communities and Local Government   may disclose the first stage information to
the Secretary of State for Work and Pensions.

6.3

Where the first stage information has been disclosed to the Secretary of State
for Work and Pensions under paragraph (2), the Secretary of State for Work and
Pensions may compare it against—

6.3.a

the name, address, date of birth and national insurance number of individuals
appearing in the following types of data kept by the Secretary of State—

6.3.a.i

data kept for the purposes of functions relating to social security (including
such information kept on behalf of the Department for Social Development), and

6.3.a.ii

data relating to working tax credit, child tax credit and child benefit (being
information kept on behalf of His Majesty’s Revenue and Customs);

6.3.b

any other information contained in such types of data which relates to the
information disclosed under paragraph (2).

6.4

The Secretary of State for Work and Pensions may disclose the results of the
comparison of the first stage information (“the second stage information”) to
the Secretary  of State  for   Housing, Communities and Local Government .

6.5

On receipt of the second stage information, the Secretary of State for
Housing, Communities and Local Government   may disclose that information—

6.5.a

to the Secretary of State for Work and Pensions, or

6.5.b

to the registration officer to whom the identity document application has been
made, or, as the case may be, to whom the Secretary of State has sent the
application under regulation  5(3) .

6.6

Paragraph (3) applies to the second stage information where it has been
disclosed to the Secretary of State for Work and Pensions under paragraph
(5)(a) as it applies to the first stage information disclosed under paragraph
(2).

6.7

The Secretary of State for Work and Pensions may disclose the results of the
comparison of the second stage information (“the third stage information”) to
the Secretary  of State   for   Housing, Communities and Local Government .

6.8

On receipt of the third stage information, the Secretary of State for
Housing, Communities and Local Government   may—

6.8.a

compare the third stage information against the information provided in the
identity document application, and

6.8.b

notify the registration officer to whom the identity document application has
been made or, as the case may be, to whom the Secretary of State has sent the
application under regulation  5(3) , as to whether the comparison in sub-
paragraph (a) resulted in a match.

6.9

The registration officer must take into account any information disclosed by,
or notification received from, the Secretary of State for   Housing,
Communities and Local Government   in accordance with this regulation when
determining the identity document application.

6.10

This regulation does not apply where—

6.10.a

the applicant—

6.10.a.i

makes an application under section 10ZC or 10ZD of the 1983 Act at the same
time as the identity document application,

6.10.a.ii

the name, date of birth and national insurance number of the applicant are
disclosed in accordance with   or 29ZAA(3)   of the Representation of the
People (England and Wales) Regulations 2001  or   or 29ZAA(3)   of the
Representation of the People (Scotland) Regulations 2001 , and

6.10.a.iii

the name, date of birth and national insurance number disclosed are identical
to the name, date of birth and national insurance number provided by the
applicant in the identity document application;

6.10.b

the applicant—

6.10.b.i

is under the age of 16, or

6.10.b.ii

does not provide both a date of birth and a national insurance number in
accordance with regulation  4(1)(d)  and (e) respectively.

6.11

Where paragraph  (10)(a)  applies, the registration officer must take into
account any results disclosed by the Secretary of State for   Housing,
Communities and Local Government   in accordance with regulation 29ZA  or
29ZAA   of the Representation of the People (England and Wales) Regulations
2001 or (as the case may be) with regulation 29ZA  or 29ZAA   of the
Representation of the People (Scotland) Regulations 2001 in respect of the
application described in paragraph  (10)(a)(i)  when determining the identity
document application.

6.12

In paragraph (1)—

“ infrastructure system ” has the meaning given in Schedule 3A to the
Communications Act 2003 ; “ relevant address ” means the address provided by
the applicant in accordance with regulation  4(1)(b) .

#### Power to request additional evidence where certain information is unavailable or where the registration officer considers it necessary

7

7.1

A registration officer must require an applicant to provide additional
evidence where the registration officer considers additional evidence is
necessary to verify the identity of the applicant in respect of their identity
document application, including where the officer considers it is necessary
because the applicant is not able to state the information required by
regulation  4(1)(d)  or (e).

7.2

Where a registration officer requires additional evidence—

7.2.a

the officer must, at the same time, inform the applicant of—

7.2.a.i

the evidence submission date, which is the date 28 days after the day on which
the registration officer requires the additional evidence, and

7.2.a.ii

the fact that the registration officer may reject the applicant’s identity
document application in the event that the applicant fails or refuses to
provide the additional evidence on or before the evidence submission date; and

7.2.b

if the applicant provides additional evidence, it must be provided in
accordance with—

7.2.b.i

where the applicant has or is applying to have an anonymous entry on the
register of parliamentary electors or local government electors, one of
paragraphs (3) to (6);

7.2.b.ii

otherwise, one of paragraphs (4) to (6).

7.3

The applicant may provide a copy, or where the registration officer considers
it appropriate, the original, of one of the following documents—

7.3.a

the applicant’s passport;

7.3.b

the applicant’s identity card issued in the European Economic Area;

7.3.c

the applicant’s biometric immigration document issued in the United Kingdom in
accordance with regulations made under section 5 of the Borders Act 2007 ;

7.3.d

the applicant’s electoral identity card issued in Northern Ireland;

7.3.e

the applicant’s photocard driving licence granted in the United Kingdom or
driving licence granted by a Crown Dependency, which bears a photograph of the
applicant.

7.4

The applicant may provide a copy, or where the registration officer considers
it appropriate, the original of—

7.4.a

one of the following documents, which, except in relation to paragraph (vii)
must have been issued in the United Kingdom or Crown Dependencies—

7.4.a.i

the applicant’s birth certificate;

7.4.a.ii

the applicant’s marriage or civil partnership certificate;

7.4.a.iii

the applicant’s adoption certificate;

7.4.a.iv

the applicant’s firearms certificate granted under the Firearms Act 1968 ;

7.4.a.v

the record of a decision on bail made in respect of the applicant in
accordance with section 5(1) of the Bail Act 1976 ;

7.4.a.vi

the applicant’s driving licence, which is not in the form of a photocard;

7.4.a.vii

the applicant’s driving licence, granted other than in the United Kingdom or
Crown Dependencies, which bears a photograph of the applicant and which must
be valid for at least 12 months from the date the applicant entered the United
Kingdom; and

7.4.b

two other documents, each of which may be either from sub-paragraph (a) or
paragraph (5).

7.5

The applicant may provide a copy, or where the registration officer considers
it appropriate, the original, of four documents, each of which may be any of
the following kinds of evidence and which must bear the applicant’s full name
as stated on the identify document application—

7.5.a

a financial statement, including but not limited to—

7.5.a.i

a mortgage statement;

7.5.a.ii

a bank or building society statement or a letter from a bank or building
society confirming that the applicant has opened an account with that bank or
building society;

7.5.a.iii

a credit card statement;

7.5.a.iv

a pension statement;

7.5.b

a council tax demand letter or statement;

7.5.c

a utility bill;

7.5.d

a Form P45 or Form P60 issued to the applicant by their employer or former
employer;

7.5.e

a statement of benefits or entitlement to benefits, such as a statement of
child benefit, within the meaning of section 141 of the Social Security
Contributions and Benefits Act 1992 , or a letter confirming that the
applicant is entitled to housing benefit, within the meaning of section 130 of
that Act .

7.6

The applicant may provide an attestation which must—

7.6.a

confirm that the applicant is the person named in the identity document
application,

7.6.b

state that the qualifying attestor is aware of the penalty for providing false
information to a registration officer,

7.6.c

be in writing and signed by the qualifying attestor,

7.6.d

state the full name, date of birth, address, electoral number and occupation
of the qualifying attestor, and

7.6.e

state the date on which it is made.

7.7

In paragraph (6), the “qualifying attestor” is a person—

7.7.a

whom the registration officer is satisfied is of good standing in the
community,

7.7.b

who is registered as an elector—

7.7.b.i

where the registration officer to whom the application is made is appointed
for an area in England or Wales, in a local authority area in England or
Wales,

7.7.b.ii

where the registration officer to whom the application is made is appointed
for an area in Scotland, in a local authority area in Scotland,

7.7.c

who is not the spouse, civil partner, parent, grandparent, brother, sister,
child or grandchild of the applicant, and

7.7.ca

regulation 25A(3) of the Representation of the People (Northern Ireland)
Regulations 2008;

7.7.d

who has not already signed   a relevant identity attestation   for two
applicants since, whichever is the later of,—

7.7.d.i

the date on which the revised register in which that person’s name appears was
last published under section 13(1) of the 1983 Act , or

7.7.d.ii

the date on which a notice specifying that person’s entry in the register was
issued under (as the case may be) section 13A(2), 13AB(2), 13B(3), (3B) or
(3D) or 13BC(3) or (6) of that Act  (and if there has been more than one such
notice, the date on which the last one was issued).

7.7A

In paragraph (7)(d), a relevant identity attestation is an attestation
provided in accordance with—

7.7A.a

paragraph (6);

7.7A.b

regulation   26B(6) or (6ZA) or 56C(5A) or (6)   of the Representation of the
People (England and Wales) Regulations 2001;

7.7A.c

regulation   26B(6) or (6ZA) or 56C(5A) or (6)   of the Representation of the
People (Scotland) Regulations 2001;

7.7A.d

paragraph 16C(5) of Schedule 2 to the Police and Crime Commissioner Elections
Order 2012;

7.7A.e

regulation   72B(5A) or (6)   of the Recall of MPs Act 2015 (Recall Petition)
Regulations 2016.

7.8

This regulation does not apply where—

7.8.a

the applicant is under the age of 16,

7.8.b

there is information available to the registration officer from any
educational record relating to the applicant, and

7.8.c

that information is sufficient to satisfy the registration officer as to the
applicant’s identity.

7.9

In this regulation, “ Crown Dependency ” means the Bailiwick of Jersey, the
Bailiwick of Guernsey or the Isle of Man.

#### Registration officer’s right to inspect certain records

8

8.1

A registration officer is authorised to inspect, for the purpose of
determining identity document applications, records kept (in whatever form)
by—

8.1.a

an authority listed in paragraph (2), or

8.1.b

any person providing services to, or authorised to exercise any function of,
any such authority.

8.2

Those authorities are—

8.2.a

the council by which the registration officer was appointed,

8.2.b

where the council by which the registration officer was appointed is a council
for a district in a county for which there is a county council, that county
council, and

8.2.c

any superintendent registrar of births, deaths and marriages, registrar of
births and deaths or registrar of marriages.

8.3

A registration officer is authorised to make copies of information contained
in such records.

#### Power to require information

9

9.1

A registration officer may require any person to give information required for
the purpose of determining an identity document application.

9.2

A registration officer may not use the power conferred by paragraph (1) to
require an applicant to provide information to assist the registration officer
in determining, in connection with that person’s application, whether that
applicant is the person named in that application.

9.3

If a person fails to comply with a requisition under paragraph (1), that
person is liable on summary conviction to a fine not exceeding level 3 on the
standard scale.

### Determination of applications

#### Postponement of determination of identity document applications

10

10.1

Where an identity document application is received by a registration officer
during the postponement period for a relevant election, petition or referendum
held in the area for which the registration officer is appointed, the
registration officer—

10.1.a

must not determine the application in accordance with regulation  11(2)
before the postponement date, and

10.1.b

subject to paragraph (2), must notify the applicant that the application will
not be determined before that date.

10.2

Paragraph (1)(b) does not apply where the application is received by the
registration officer on the postponement date.

10.3

In this regulation—

10.3.a

the “ postponement date ” in relation to a relevant election, petition or
referendum means—

10.3.a.i

the relevant date of that election, petition or referendum, or

10.3.a.ii

where the date under paragraph (i) falls within the postponement period for a
subsequent relevant election, petition or referendum held in the area for
which the registration officer is appointed, the working day before the date
under paragraph (i);

10.3.b

the “postponement period” for a relevant election, petition or referendum is
the period—

10.3.b.i

beginning at 5pm on the sixth working day before the relevant date, and

10.3.b.ii

ending at 10pm on the relevant date;

10.3.c

the “ relevant date ” in relation to a relevant election, petition or
referendum means the day of the poll or, in the case of a recall petition, the
last day of the signing period for that petition;

10.3.d

“ working day ” means any day other than a Saturday, Sunday, Good Friday,
Christmas Eve, Christmas Day or a bank holiday.

#### Determination of identity document applications

11

11.1

A registration officer may refuse an identity document application where—

11.1.a

the registration officer has required the applicant to provide additional
evidence in accordance with regulation  7 , and

11.1.b

the applicant has failed or refused to comply with that requirement on or
before the evidence submission date described in regulation  7(2)(a)(i) .

11.2

Except where an identity document application is refused in accordance with
paragraph (1), the registration officer must—

11.2.a

grant an identity document application if the registration officer is
satisfied that the following conditions are met—

11.2.a.i

conditions 1 and 2, and

11.2.a.ii

either condition 3 or 4, or

11.2.b

refuse the application if not so satisfied.

11.3

Condition 1 is that the application meets the requirements set out in
regulation  4(1)  to (3).

11.4

Condition 2 is that the applicant is the person named in the application.

11.5

Condition 3 is that—

11.5.a

the applicant is registered in a register of parliamentary electors in Great
Britain, or a register of local government electors in England, which is
maintained by the registration officer, or

11.5.b

the registration officer is required to enter the applicant in such a register
in accordance with section 10ZC(1) of the 1983 Act.

11.6

Condition 4 is that—

11.6.a

either—

11.6.a.i

the applicant is registered in a register of local government electors in
Wales which is maintained by the registration officer, or

11.6.a.ii

the registration officer is required to enter the applicant in that register
in accordance with section 10ZC(1) of the 1983 Act, and

11.6.b

the applicant is entitled to vote at an election of a police and crime
commissioner for a police area in Wales in accordance with section 52(1A) of
the Police Reform and Social Responsibility Act 2011 , or will be so entitled
on attaining the age of 18.

#### Notification following determination

12

12.1

Where a registration officer grants or refuses an identity document
application, the registration officer must notify the applicant of that
determination, together with any other information required by this
regulation.

12.2

Where the registration officer grants the identity document application, the
registration officer must also notify the applicant whether the electoral
identity document or, as the case may be, the anonymous elector’s document to
be issued to the applicant will be delivered to the applicant by post or made
available for collection by the applicant, as determined in accordance with
regulation  17 .

12.3

Where the registration officer refuses an identity document application, the
registration officer must also notify the applicant of—

12.3.a

the reason for that refusal,

12.3.b

the right of appeal under section 56(1)(ac) of the 1983 Act , and

12.3.c

the time in which any notice of appeal under that section must be given (in
accordance with regulation  13(1) ).

12.4

Where the registration officer notifies the applicant other than by written
notification, the registration officer must, as soon as reasonably practicable
after that notification send a written notification containing the same
information to the relevant delivery address (which has the same meaning as in
regulation  4(7) ).

#### Appeal following determination

13

13.1

A person who wishes to appeal under section 56(1)(ac) of the 1983 Act against
the decision of a registration officer to refuse an identity document
application must give notice of the appeal to the registration officer, before
the end of the period of 14 days beginning with the day on which the
notification under regulation  12  is given, specifying the grounds of the
appeal.

13.2

Where regulation  12(4)  applies in respect of the refusal, the reference to
notification in paragraph (1) is to be read as the first notification under
regulation  12  to that person.

13.3

The registration officer must forward any such notice to the relevant court in
the manner directed by rules of court together with a statement setting out—

13.3.a

the material facts which in the registration officer’s opinion have been
established in the case,

13.3.b

the registration officer’s decision, and

13.3.c

the registration officer’s representations on any point specified as a ground
of appeal.

13.4

The registration officer must also give to the relevant court any other
information which the court may require and which the registration officer is
able to give.

13.5

Where it appears to a registration officer that any notices of appeal given to
the registration officer are based on similar grounds, the registration
officer must inform the relevant court of this to enable the court (if it
thinks fit) to consolidate the appeals or select a case as a test case.

13.6

In this regulation, “relevant court”—

13.6.a

where the registration officer is appointed for an area in England or Wales,
means the county court;

13.6.b

where the registration officer is appointed for an area in Scotland, means the
sheriff.

#### Processing of information provided in connection with an identity document application

14

14.1

If a person provides an original document under regulation  7(3) , (4) or (5),
the registration officer must make a copy of that document and return the
original document to the person who provided it.

14.2

In the remainder of this regulation, the “relevant documents and information”
in respect of an identity document application means—

14.2.a

the application form or, in the case of an application made through the
digital service, the information contained in the application  transmitted to
the registration officer by the Secretary of State , and

14.2.b

any other information or documents provided to the registration officer in
connection with the application or, in the case of original documents which
are returned under paragraph (1), a copy of such documents.

14.3

The registration officer must retain the relevant documents and information—

14.3.a

where the registration officer grants the identity document application, for
the period of 28 working days beginning with the day on which the registration
officer granted the application;

14.3.b

where the registration officer refuses the identity document application, for
the period of 12 months beginning with the day on which the registration
officer refused that application.

14.4

Information disclosed under regulation  6  must not be disclosed to any other
person, except—

14.4.a

for the purpose of determining the application in connection with which the
information was disclosed, or

14.4.b

for the purpose of any civil or criminal proceedings.

14.5

A person who discloses information in breach of paragraph  (4)  is guilty of
an offence and liable—

14.5.a

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding two
years, or to a fine (or both);

14.5.b

on summary conviction—

14.5.b.i

in England and Wales, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding the general
limit in a magistrates’ court, or to a fine (or both);

14.5.b.ii

in Scotland, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 12 months or to a fine
not exceeding the statutory maximum (or both).

14.6

Any information disclosed under regulation  6  must be processed in accordance
with any requirements as to the processing of information that may have been
imposed by the Secretary of State for   Housing, Communities and Local
Government   in writing in advance of that processing, including requirements
as to the transfer, storage, destruction and security of that information.

14.7

In this regulation—

“ copy ” includes an electronic copy; “ working day ” means any day other than
a Saturday, Sunday, Good Friday, Christmas Eve, Christmas Day or a bank
holiday; “ bank holiday ” means— where the registration officer is appointed
for an area in England or Wales, a day which is a bank holiday under the
Banking and Financial Dealings Act 1971 in England and Wales; where the
registration officer is appointed for an area in Scotland, a day which is a
bank holiday under the Banking and Financial Dealings Act 1971 in Scotland.

### Design, issuing, delivery, collection etc. of electoral identity documents, anonymous elector’s documents etc.

#### Design of documents

##### Design of electoral identity documents, anonymous elector’s documents, etc.

15

15.1

The Electoral Commission must design the following—

15.1.a

an anonymous elector’s document;

15.1.b

an electoral identity document;

15.1.c

a temporary electoral identity document;

15.1.d

a dual Welsh and English version of each of the designs referred to in sub-
paragraphs (a) to (c).

15.2

A document designed by the Electoral Commission in accordance with paragraph
(1) must meet the requirements for that document as set out in Schedule 3.

15.3

The Electoral Commission must make available—

15.3.a

each of the designs referred to in paragraph (1)(a) to (c) to a registration
officer who is appointed for an area in England or Scotland;

15.3.b

the dual Welsh and English version of each of the designs referred to in
paragraph (1)(a) to (c) to a registration officer who is appointed for an area
in Wales.

15.4

The Electoral Commission may design a revised version of a document designed
in accordance with paragraph (1), and where the Electoral Commission does so—

15.4.a

paragraphs (2) and (3) apply to a revised version as they apply to the
document designed in accordance with paragraph (1), and

15.4.b

the design of a revised version of a document referred to in paragraph (1)
does not invalidate any previous version of the document issued under these
Regulations before the day on which the revised version is made available to
the registration officer.

#### Issuing and delivery or collection of electoral identity documents and anonymous elector’s documents

##### Issuing of electoral identity documents and anonymous elector’s documents

16

16.1

Where the registration officer grants an identity document application, the
registration officer must issue the applicant with an electoral identity
document or, as the case may be, an anonymous elector’s document which must—

16.1.a

use the version of the design for that document most recently made available
to the registration officer in accordance with regulation  15 ,

16.1.b

state—

16.1.b.i

in the case of an electoral identity document, the applicant’s full name,

16.1.b.ii

in the case of an anonymous elector’s document, the applicant’s electoral
number,

16.1.c

contain the photograph of the applicant provided in accordance with regulation
4(3) ,

16.1.d

state the date of issue,

16.1.e

state an appropriate identifier, and

16.1.f

in the case of an electoral identity document, state—

16.1.f.i

the name of the local authority by which the registration officer is
appointed, and

16.1.f.ii

states the recommended renewal date for the document.

16.2

In paragraph  (1)(b)(ii) , the applicant’s “electoral number” is the number—

16.2.a

allocated to the applicant as stated in the register of electors, or

16.2.b

where an entry related to the applicant is added to the register in pursuance
of a notice issued under section 13A(2), 13AB(2), 13B(3), (3B) or (3D) or
13BC(3) or (6) of the 1983 Act, as stated in the copy of that notice.

16.3

In paragraph  (1)(e) , an “appropriate identifier” is an identifier made up of
up to 20 numbers or letters which—

16.3.a

is allocated by the registration officer in respect of an electoral identity
document or, as the case may be, an anonymous elector’s document, and

16.3.b

is not an identifier allocated by that registration officer in respect of any
other electoral identity document or anonymous elector’s document.

16.4

In paragraph  (1)(f)(ii) , the “recommended renewal date” for an electoral
identity document is the date which is the tenth anniversary of the date of
issue of that document.

##### Delivery or collection of issued electoral identity documents and anonymous elector’s documents

17

17.1

Subject to paragraph  (3) , the registration officer must arrange for an
electoral identity document or anonymous elector’s document issued in
accordance with regulation  16  (“the issued document”) to be delivered by
post to the applicant’s relevant delivery address (which has the meaning given
in regulation  4(7) ).

17.2

An anonymous elector’s document to which paragraph (1) applies must be
delivered in an envelope or other form of covering so as not to disclose to
any other person that the applicant has an anonymous entry.

17.3

The registration officer may arrange for the issued document to be made
available for collection by the applicant in person (instead of arranging
delivery in accordance with paragraph (1)) where—

17.3.a

an indication is given by the applicant in accordance with regulation  4(1)(f)
, and

17.3.b

the registration officer considers that it is necessary to make the issued
document available for collection to ensure that the applicant receives the
issued document.

17.4

Where an issued document is made available for collection in accordance with
paragraph  (3) , the registration officer must notify the applicant—

17.4.a

that the issued document is available to be collected,

17.4.b

of the location where, and the times during which, the issued document may be
collected, and

17.4.c

that the issued document may only be collected by the applicant in person, and

17.4.d

where the issued document is an anonymous elector’s document, that the
applicant must bring their certificate of anonymous registration when
collecting the document, and must show the certificate upon request.

17.5

Where the applicant gives an indication in accordance with regulation  4(1)(h)
, the registration officer must also arrange for a Braille, easy read or large
print explanation of the issued document to be delivered or made available for
collection (as the case may be) with the issued document.

17.6

In paragraph  (4)(d) , “ certificate of anonymous registration ” means the
certificate issued to an anonymous elector in accordance with regulation 45G
of the Representation of the People (England and Wales) Regulations 2001 or
regulation 45F of the Representation of the People (Scotland) Regulations
2001.

17.7

The registration officer may combine a notification under paragraph  (4)  with
a notification under regulation  12 .

#### Issuing of temporary electoral identity documents

##### Issuing of temporary electoral identity documents

18

18.1

This regulation applies where, at any time during the relevant period for a
relevant election, petition or referendum, a registration officer issues an
applicant with an electoral identity document in accordance with regulation
16 .

18.2

The registration officer may also issue the applicant with a temporary
electoral identity document where the registration officer is satisfied that
the issued electoral identity document may not be delivered in time to the
applicant for the applicant to be able to use that document at the relevant
election, petition or referendum.

18.3

In paragraph (1), “ the relevant period ” in relation to a relevant election,
petition or referendum means the period—

18.3.a

beginning at 5pm on the sixth working day before the relevant date, and

18.3.b

ending at—

18.3.b.i

where the relevant election, petition or referendum is a recall petition—

18.3.b.i.aa

5pm on the relevant date, or

18.3.b.i.bb

if earlier, the beginning of the final hour during which the petition will be
available for signing at the allotted petition signing place on the relevant
date;

18.3.b.ii

otherwise, 5pm on the relevant date.

18.4

In paragraph (3)—

18.4.a

“ allotted petition signing place ” means the petition signing place allotted
to the applicant in accordance with regulation 16 of the 2016 Regulations;

18.4.b

the “relevant date” is—

18.4.b.i

where the relevant election, petition or referendum is a recall petition, the
last day of the signing period for that petition;

18.4.b.ii

otherwise, the date of the poll at that election or referendum;

18.4.c

“ working day ” means any day other than a Saturday, Sunday, Good Friday,
Christmas Eve, Christmas Day or a bank holiday.

##### Temporary electoral identity documents: supplemental

19

19.1

A temporary electoral identity document issued in accordance with regulation
18  is valid only on the relevant date.

19.2

The registration officer must ensure that a temporary electoral identity
document issued to an applicant in accordance with regulation  18  (“the
issued temporary document”)—

19.2.a

use the version of the design for that document most recently made available
to the registration officer in accordance with regulation  15 ,

19.2.b

states—

19.2.b.i

the applicant’s full name,

19.2.b.ii

the date of issue,

19.2.b.iii

the name of the local authority by which the registration officer is
appointed,

19.2.b.iv

an appropriate identifier,

19.2.b.v

the date for which the issued temporary document is valid,

19.2.c

contains the photograph of the applicant provided in accordance with
regulation  4(3) , and

19.2.d

is signed by the registration officer.

19.3

In paragraph  (2)(b)(iv) , an “appropriate identifier” is an identifier made
up of up to 20 numbers or letters which—

19.3.a

is allocated by the registration officer in respect of an issued temporary
document, and

19.3.b

is not an identifier allocated by that registration officer in respect of any
other temporary electoral identity document which is valid on the same date.

19.4

The registration officer must, in relation to the issued temporary document—

19.4.a

arrange for the issued temporary document to be made available for collection
by the applicant in person,

19.4.b

notify the applicant—

19.4.b.i

that the issued temporary document is available to be collected,

19.4.b.ii

of the location where and the times during which the issued document may be
collected, and

19.4.b.iii

that the issued temporary document may only be collected by the applicant in
person, and

19.4.c

update the issued document record entry relating to the electoral identity
document referred to in regulation  18(1)  accordingly.

19.5

Where the applicant gives an indication in accordance with regulation  4(1)(h)
, the registration officer must also arrange for a Braille, easy read or large
print explanation of the issued temporary document to be made available for
collection with the issued temporary document.

19.6

The registration officer may combine a notification under paragraph (4)(b)
with a notification under regulation  12 .

19.7

In paragraph (1), “ the relevant date ” has the meaning given in regulation
18(4)(b) .

#### Record of issued documents

##### Record of anonymous elector’s documents and electoral identity documents

20

20.1

A registration officer must keep a record of all anonymous elector’s documents
and electoral identity documents issued by the registration officer (in this
Chapter, “the record”).

20.2

The registration officer must—

20.2.a

as soon as reasonably practicable after issuing an anonymous elector’s
document or electoral identity document in accordance with regulation  16 , 29
or  30(3) , make an entry in the record for that document;

20.2.b

keep entries related to electoral identity documents in a separate part of the
record from those related to anonymous elector’s documents.

20.3

An entry made in accordance with paragraph  (2)(a)  must contain the
following—

20.3.a

the date of issue and the appropriate identifier of the document;

20.3.b

the full name of the person to whom the document was issued;

20.3.c

the address provided by the person in accordance with regulation  4(1)(b) ;

20.3.d

any address provided by the person in accordance with regulation  4(1)(c) ;

20.3.e

any indication given by the person in accordance with regulation  4(1)(f) ;

20.3.f

any indication given by the person in accordance with regulation  4(1)(h) ;

20.3.g

a copy of the person’s photograph provided in accordance with regulation  4(3)
;

20.3.h

any email address or telephone number provided in accordance with regulation
4(4) ;

20.3.i

in respect of an electoral identity document, the name of the local authority
by which the registration officer is appointed;

20.3.j

an indication of whether a temporary electoral identity document was also
issued in accordance with regulation  18 , and if so—

20.3.j.i

the appropriate identifier of that temporary electoral identity document, and

20.3.j.ii

the relevant date (which has the meaning given in regulation  18(4)(b) ).

20.4

Where—

20.4.a

an anonymous elector’s document is issued in accordance with regulation 29 or
30(3) , the reference in paragraph  (3)(g)  to a photograph provided in
accordance with regulation  4(3)  is to be read as a reference to the
photograph contained in the issued document record entry for the anonymous
elector’s document referred to in regulation  27(1)(a)  or  30(1)(a)  (as the
case may be);

20.4.b

an anonymous elector’s document is issued in accordance with regulation 29—

20.4.b.i

the reference in paragraph  (3)(c)  to the address provided in accordance with
regulation  4(1)(b)  is to be read as a reference to the address referred to
in regulation  29(4)(a)(ii)(cc) ;

20.4.b.ii

the reference in paragraph  (3)(d)  to any address provided in accordance with
regulation  4(1)(c)  is to be read as a reference to an address referred to in
regulation  29(4)(a)(ii)(aa)  or (bb);

20.4.b.iii

the reference in paragraph  (3)(e)  to regulation  4(1)(f)  is to be read as a
reference to regulation  28(d) .

20.5

The registration officer must—

20.5.a

delete any information included in an entry in accordance with paragraph
(3)(c)  to (f) and (h) at the end of the first retention period for that
entry;

20.5.b

delete any information included in an entry in accordance with paragraph
(3)(j)  at the end of the second retention period for that entry;

20.5.c

delete an entry from the record at the end of the third retention period for
that entry.

20.6

In paragraph (5), in relation to an entry in the record—

20.6.a

“the first retention period” is the period beginning with the day on which the
entry is made and ending—

20.6.a.i

where the entry relates to an electoral identity document, ending with the day
which is 28 working days after the date of issue for that document;

20.6.a.ii

where the entry relates to an anonymous elector’s document, ending with the
day which is 15 months after the date of issue for that document;

20.6.b

“the second retention period” is the period beginning with the day on which
the entry is made and ending on the second 1st July following the date of
issue for the electoral identity document to which the entry relates;

20.6.c

“the third retention period” is the period beginning with the day on which the
entry is made and ending on the tenth 1st July following the date of issue for
the anonymous elector’s document or electoral identity document to which the
entry relates.

20.7

In paragraph (6)(a)(i), “ working day ” means any day other than a Saturday,
Sunday, Good Friday, Christmas Eve, Christmas Day or a bank holiday; and for
these purposes “ bank holiday ” has the meaning given in regulation  14(7) .

##### Duties of registration officer and staff in relation to the record

21

21.1

This regulation applies to—

21.1.a

a registration officer,

21.1.b

a deputy registration officer, and

21.1.c

any person appointed to assist any such officer or who in the course of the
person’s employment is assigned to assist such officer in that officer’s
functions under section 13BD or 13BE of the 1983 Act.

21.2

Where a registration officer is also the relevant officer at any relevant
election, petition or referendum, this regulation applies to—

21.2.a

the registration officer acting in that capacity,

21.2.b

any person appointed as a deputy to the registration officer acting in that
capacity, and

21.2.c

any person appointed to assist a person mentioned in sub-paragraph (a) or (b)
or who in the course of the person’s employment is assigned to assist a person
mentioned in sub-paragraph (a) or (b) in respect of the relevant election,
petition or referendum in question.

21.3

This regulation also applies to a person—

21.3.a

to whom a copy of the record is supplied or information from the record is
disclosed in accordance with paragraph (4), and

21.3.b

who is not a person to whom this regulation applies by virtue of paragraph (1)
or (2).

21.4

A person to whom this regulation applies must not—

21.4.a

supply to any person a copy of the record,

21.4.b

disclose information contained in it, or

21.4.c

make use of such information,

otherwise than in accordance with an enactment (including these Regulations)
or the order of any court or tribunal made at any hearing or during the course
of any proceedings.

21.5

Nothing in paragraph (4) applies to the supply or disclosure by a person to
whom this regulation applies to another such person in connection with either
person’s functions under section 13BD or 13BE of the 1983 Act or for the
purposes of a relevant election, petition or referendum.

21.6

A person to whom this regulation applies must take proper precautions for the
safe custody of the record.

21.7

In paragraph (4), “ enactment ” has the same meaning as in section 17(2) of
the Representation of the People Act 2000 .

21.8

In this regulation and in regulations  22  and  23 , “ record ” includes a
part of the record.

##### Supply, disclosure and use of record for the purposes of relevant elections, petitions and referendums

22

22.1

A registration officer may upon request supply a copy of the record to a
relevant officer for the purposes of a relevant election, petition or
referendum.

22.2

A person to whom a copy of the record has been supplied under this regulation
must not—

22.2.a

supply to any person a copy of the record,

22.2.b

disclose any information contained in it, or

22.2.c

make use of any such information,

other than for the purposes of a relevant election, petition or referendum (as
the case may be).

22.3

Each person supplied with a copy of the record under this regulation must take
proper precautions for its safe custody.

##### Supply of the record to police forces and other organisations

23

23.1

Subject to paragraph (2), a registration officer must upon request supply a
copy of the record to—

23.1.a

any police force in Great Britain,

23.1.b

the Police Service of Northern Ireland or the Police Service of Northern
Ireland (Reserve),

23.1.c

any body of constables established under an Act, or

23.1.d

the National Crime Agency.

23.2

The registration officer must not supply a copy of the record in accordance
with paragraph (1) where that record contains the whole or part of an issued
document record entry relating to an anonymous elector’s document unless the
request is made in writing by—

23.2.a

in the case of forces and organisations mentioned in paragraph (1)(a) to (c),
an officer of a rank senior to that of superintendent;

23.2.b

in the case of the National Crime Agency, the Director General of that Agency.

23.3

A constable, officer or employee of any of the forces or organisations
mentioned in paragraph (1) must not—

23.3.a

supply to any person a copy of the record,

23.3.b

disclose any information contained in it, or

23.3.c

make use of any such information,

otherwise than for the purposes of the prevention and detection of crime and
the enforcement of the criminal law (whether in England and Wales or Scotland
or elsewhere).

23.4

Each person supplied with a copy of the record under this regulation must take
proper precautions for its safe custody.

23.5

Paragraphs (3) and (4) also apply to a person—

23.5.a

to whom a copy of the record is supplied or information from the record is
disclosed in accordance with paragraph (3), and

23.5.b

who is not a constable, officer or employee of any of the forces or
organisations mentioned in paragraph (1);

as those paragraphs apply to such a constable, officer or employee.

##### Offence in respect of contravention of regulation 21(4) or (6), 

24

24.1

A person (“ B ”) who fails to comply with regulation  21(4)  or (6) or  22(2)
or (3) is guilty of an offence and is liable on summary conviction—

24.1.a

in England and Wales, to a fine;

24.1.b

in Scotland, to a fine not exceeding the statutory maximum.

24.2

A person (“ B ”) who fails to comply with regulation  23(3)  or (4) is guilty
of an offence and is liable on summary conviction—

24.2.a

in England and Wales, to a fine;

24.2.b

in Scotland or Northern Ireland, to a fine not exceeding the statutory
maximum.

24.3

It is a defence for B to show that B took all reasonable steps to comply with
regulation  21(4)  or (6),  22(2)  or (3) or  23(3)  or (4) (as the case may
be).

### Anonymous elector’s documents: reminders and replacement

#### Reminders

##### Reminder of the need for an anonymous elector’s document: general

25

25.1

In this regulation and in regulation  26 , a “reminder” is a notice to a
person stating that they must have an anonymous elector’s document in order
to—

25.1.a

vote in person as an anonymous elector at a relevant election, petition or
referendum other than a recall petition, or

25.1.b

sign a signing sheet as a person with an anonymous entry in the register at a
recall petition.

25.2

A registration officer must send a reminder to—

25.2.a

a person as soon as reasonably practicable after the registration officer
makes an anonymous entry in a register of parliamentary electors or a register
of local government electors in England or Wales for that person in accordance
with section 9B(3)(b) of the 1983 Act ;

25.2.b

a qualifying anonymous elector during the relevant period.

25.3

Paragraph (2)(a) does not apply to a person who—

25.3.a

has an anonymous entry in a register of local government electors in Wales,
and

25.3.b

is not entitled to vote at a PCC election for a police area in Wales in
accordance with section 52(1A) of the Police Reform and Social Responsibility
Act 2011.

25.4

In paragraph (2)(b), a “qualifying anonymous elector” is a person who—

25.4.a

has an anonymous entry in—

25.4.a.i

a register of parliamentary electors,

25.4.a.ii

a register of local government electors in England, or

25.4.a.iii

a register of local government electors in Wales and that person is entitled
to vote at a PCC election for a police area in Wales in accordance with
section 52(1A) of the Police Reform and Social Responsibility Act 2011;

25.4.b

has not been issued with an anonymous elector’s document at any time between
the date on which that anonymous entry first takes effect and the beginning of
the relevant period, and

25.4.c

in the event of a relevant election, petition or referendum other than a
recall petition, would not have an entry in the postal voters list or the list
of proxies.

25.5

The registration officer may combine a reminder under paragraph (1)(b) with a
reminder under regulation 25A(2) of the Representation of the People (England
and Wales) Regulations 2001 or regulation 25A(2) of the Representation of the
People (Scotland) Regulations 2001 (reminder of termination of registration of
person with anonymous entry).

25.6

In this regulation—

25.6.a

“ the list of proxies ” means the list of persons kept in pursuance of—

25.6.a.i

in relation to a relevant election, petition or referendum which is a PCC
election, paragraph 4(3) of Schedule 2 to the Police and Crime Commissioner
Elections Order 2012;

25.6.a.ii

otherwise, paragraph 5(3) of Schedule 4 to the Representation of the People
Act 2000;

25.6.b

“ the postal voters list ” means the list of persons kept in pursuance of—

25.6.b.i

in relation to a relevant election, petition or referendum which is a PCC
election, paragraph 4(2) of Schedule 2 to the Police and Crime Commissioner
Elections Order 2012;

25.6.b.ii

otherwise, paragraph 5(2) of Schedule 4 to the Representation of the People
Act 2000 ;

25.6.c

“ the relevant period ” means the period—

25.6.c.i

beginning with the day which is nine months after the day on which the
person’s anonymous entry first takes effect, and

25.6.c.ii

ending with the day which is ten months after the day on which that entry
first takes effect.

##### Reminder of the need for an anonymous elector’s document: transitional provision

26

26.1

Subject to paragraph (2), a registration officer must send a reminder to all
qualifying anonymous electors registered in a register for which the
registration officer is appointed no later than the end of the period of two
months beginning with the day on which this regulation comes into force.

26.2

Paragraph (1) does not apply in respect of a qualifying anonymous elector
where, during the period described in paragraph (1)—

26.2.a

the qualifying anonymous elector’s entry is removed from the register of
electors in accordance with section 9C of the 1983 Act ;

26.2.b

the registration officer sends a reminder to the qualifying anonymous elector
in accordance with regulation  25 .

26.3

In this regulation, a “ qualifying anonymous elector ” means a person who, on
the day on which this regulation comes into force, has an anonymous entry in—

26.3.a

a register of parliamentary electors,

26.3.b

a register of local government electors in England, or

26.3.c

a register of local government electors in Wales and that person is entitled
to vote at a PCC election for a police area in Wales in accordance with
section 52(1A) of the Police Reform and Social Responsibility Act 2011.

#### Replacement of anonymous elector’s documents: change of electoral number

##### Application and interpretation of Chapter 2

27

27.1

This Chapter applies where—

27.1.a

a person has been issued with an anonymous elector’s document in accordance
with these Regulations, and

27.1.b

the person is allocated an electoral number which is different from the one
shown on that document, other than as the result of an application under
section 9B of the 1983 Act (anonymous registration).

27.2

In this Chapter, “ electoral number ” has the same meaning as in regulation
16(2) .

##### Notification as to replacement

28

The registration officer must notify a person to whom this Chapter applies
that—

28.a

the person’s electoral number has changed,

28.b

the anonymous elector’s document previously issued to the person is no longer
valid as a result,

28.c

the registration officer intends to issue the person with a new anonymous
elector’s document, and

28.d

the person may notify the registration officer if the person considers that it
is necessary to collect the document in person from the registration officer
instead of the document being delivered by post, and the reason why the person
considers that collection is necessary.

##### Replacement of anonymous elector’s document following change of electoral number

29

29.1

A registration officer must issue a person to whom this Chapter applies by
virtue of regulation  27(1)  with a new anonymous elector’s document and
regulations  16(1)  and  17  apply in relation to the issue of the new
document as those regulations apply following the granting of an identity
document application in accordance with regulation  11(2)(a) , subject to the
modifications set out in paragraphs (2) to (4).

29.2

References to the applicant are to be read as references to the person issued
with a document under this regulation.

29.3

In regulation  16(1)(c) , the reference to the photograph of the applicant is
to be read as a reference to the photograph of the person contained in the
issued document record entry relating to the anonymous elector’s document
described in regulation  27(1)(a) .

29.4

In regulation  17 —

29.4.a

in paragraph (1)—

29.4.a.i

the reference to regulation  16  is to be read as a reference to this
regulation;

29.4.a.ii

the reference to the applicant’s relevant delivery address is to be read as a
reference to—

29.4.a.ii.aa

where the person is registered in pursuance of a service declaration, the
person’s present address, correspondence address or British Forces Post Office
Number;

29.4.a.ii.bb

where the person is registered in pursuance of an overseas elector’s
declaration, the person’s present address;

29.4.a.ii.cc

otherwise, the address in respect of which the person is registered as an
elector;

29.4.b

in paragraph (3)(a), the reference to regulation  4(1)(f)  is to be read as a
reference to regulation 28(d);

29.4.c

in paragraph (7), the reference to a notification under regulation  12  is to
be read as a reference to a notification under regulation  28 .

#### Replacement of anonymous elector’s documents following loss etc. of document

##### Replacement of anonymous elector’s document following loss etc. of document

30

30.1

This regulation applies where—

30.1.a

a person (“ P ”) has been issued with an anonymous elector’s document in
accordance with these Regulations,

30.1.b

P intends to use that document as a specified document at a relevant election,
petition or referendum, and

30.1.c

during the replacement period for that relevant election, petition or
referendum the document is lost, stolen, destroyed or damaged so as to be no
longer usable as a specified document.

30.2

Where this regulation applies, P may make a request during the replacement
period to the registration officer for a replacement anonymous elector’s
document.

30.3

Where P makes a request in accordance with paragraph (2), the registration
officer must issue a replacement anonymous elector’s document (“the
replacement document”), and regulation  16(1)  applies in relation to the
issue of the replacement document as that regulation applies following the
granting of an identity document application in accordance with regulation
11(2)(a) , subject to the following modifications—

30.3.a

references to the applicant are to be read as references to P;

30.3.b

in regulation  16(1)(c) , the reference to the photograph of the applicant is
to be read as a reference to the photograph of P contained in the issued
document record entry relating to the anonymous elector’s document described
in paragraph  (1)(a) .

30.4

The registration officer must—

30.4.a

arrange for the replacement document to be made available for collection by P
in person, and

30.4.b

notify P—

30.4.b.i

that the replacement document is available to be collected,

30.4.b.ii

of the location where and the times during which the replacement document may
be collected,

30.4.b.iii

that the replacement document may only be collected by P in person, and

30.4.b.iv

that when collecting the issued document P must bring their certificate of
anonymous registration and must show the certificate upon request.

30.5

Where the issued document record entry relating to the anonymous elector’s
document described in paragraph  (1)(a)  contains information described in
regulation  20(3)(f) , the registration officer must also arrange for a
Braille, easy read or large print explanation of the replacement document to
be made available for collection with the replacement document.

30.6

In this regulation—

30.6.a

“ certificate of anonymous registration ” has the same meaning as in
regulation  17(6) ;

30.6.b

the “replacement period”, in respect of a relevant election, petition or
referendum means the period—

30.6.b.i

beginning at 5pm on the sixth working day before the relevant date, and

30.6.b.ii

ending at the relevant time on the relevant date.

30.7

For the purposes of paragraph (6)(b)—

30.7.a

the “ relevant date ” means—

30.7.a.i

where the relevant election, petition or referendum is a recall petition, the
last day of the signing period for that petition;

30.7.a.ii

otherwise, the day of the poll at that election or referendum;

30.7.b

the “relevant time” on the relevant date means—

30.7.b.i

5pm, or

30.7.b.ii

if earlier, where the relevant election, petition or referendum is a recall
petition, the beginning of the final hour during which the petition will be
available for signing at the allotted petition signing place on that day;

30.7.c

“ working day ” means any day other than a Saturday, Sunday, Good Friday,
Christmas Eve, Christmas Day or a bank holiday.

30.8

In paragraph (7)(b), “ allotted petition signing place ” means the petition
signing place allotted to P in accordance with regulation 16 of the 2016
Regulations.

### Ballot paper refusal lists and signing sheet refusal lists

#### Ballot paper refusal list at parliamentary elections

31

For the purposes of rule 29(3ZA) of Schedule 1 to the 1983 Act (parliamentary
election rules: equipment of polling stations) , the prescribed form of the
ballot paper refusal list is the form set out in Schedule 4.

#### Inspection etc. of the completed ballot paper refusal list or signing sheet refusal list

32

32.1

This regulation applies where—

32.1.a

a person (“ A ”) requests a ballot paper or signing sheet (as the case may be)
at a relevant election, petition or referendum—

32.1.a.i

to vote at the election or referendum, or to sign the recall petition as proxy
on behalf of another person (“ B ”), or

32.1.a.ii

otherwise, to vote at the election or referendum or to sign the recall
petition, and

32.1.b

A is refused that ballot paper or signing sheet in accordance with rule 35(3)
or 37(1E) of the elections rules (including rule 37(1E) as applied by rule 38,
39 or 40 of the elections rules).

32.2

Where conditions 1 to 4 in this regulation are met, the list officer may—

32.2.a

open the sealed packet containing the completed ballot paper refusal list or
completed signing sheet refusal list (as the case may be) for that relevant
election, petition or referendum,

32.2.b

inspect the list, and

32.2.c

disclose to A, B or the relevant officer (as the case may be) the information
relating to A’s refusal.

32.3

Condition 1 is that a person requests disclosure of the information relating
to A’s refusal from either—

32.3.a

the list officer, or

32.3.b

the relevant officer for the relevant election, petition or referendum, and
the relevant officer requests disclosure of that information from the list
officer.

32.4

Condition 2 is that the request for disclosure is made before the destruction
of the completed ballot paper refusal list or completed signing sheet refusal
list (as the case may be) in accordance with rule 57(1) of the elections
rules.

32.5

Condition 3 is that the person requesting disclosure appears to the list
officer or the relevant officer to be A or B (as the case may be).

32.6

Condition 4 is that A or B (as the case may be) provides to the list officer,
or provides to the relevant officer and the relevant officer provides to the
list officer, the following—

32.6.a

where paragraph  (1)(a)(i)  applies, A’s name and address;

32.6.b

where paragraph  (1)(a)(ii)  applies, A’s electoral number.

32.7

The list officer must—

32.7.a

when opening the sealed packet and inspecting the completed ballot paper
refusal list or signing sheet refusal list, ensure that no person other than
the list officer can see any information contained in the list, and

32.7.b

must re-seal the packet containing the completed ballot paper refusal list or
signing sheet refusal list after inspecting the list in accordance with
paragraph (2)(b).

32.8

Where the list officer discloses the information relating to A’s refusal to
the relevant officer in accordance with paragraph (2)(c), the relevant
officer—

32.8.a

must disclose that information to A or B (as the case may be), and

32.8.b

must not disclose that information to any other person.

32.9

In this regulation—

32.9.a

“ electoral number ” has the meaning given in rule 40ZB(8) of the elections
rules;

32.9.b

the “ information relating to A’s refusal ” means—

32.9.b.i

the reason for the refusal to deliver—

32.9.b.i.aa

a ballot paper to A, as recorded on the completed ballot paper refusal list in
accordance with rule 40ZB(2)(b) or (3)(b) of the elections rules, or

32.9.b.i.bb

a signing sheet to A, as recorded on the completed signing sheet refusal list
in accordance with regulation 30A(2)(b) or (3)(b) of the 2016 Regulations, and

32.9.b.ii

any note relating to A which is added to such a list in accordance with rule
40ZB(5) or (6) of the elections rules;

32.9.c

“list officer”—

32.9.c.i

in respect of a recall petition in England or Wales, means the registration
officer described in regulation 44(3)(a) of the 2016 Regulations;

32.9.c.ii

in respect of a relevant election, petition or referendum in England or Wales
other than a recall petition, means the relevant registration officer as
defined by rule 55(1A) of the elections rules;

32.9.c.iii

in respect of a relevant election, petition or referendum in Scotland, means
the relevant officer;

32.9.d

“ relevant election, petition or referendum ” does not include a parliamentary
general election to which paragraph 18 of Schedule 1 to the Elections Act 2022
does not apply.

### Rule 40B of the elections rules: collection and collation of information

#### Application of rule 40B of the parliamentary election rules

33

Rule 40B of Schedule 1 to the 1983 Act (collection and disclosure of
information relating to applications made under rules 37 to 40)  applies in
relation to a parliamentary general election described in section 59A(2) of
the 1983 Act .

#### Collection of information by the presiding officer

34

34.1

This regulation and regulation  35  apply in relation to—

34.1.a

a parliamentary general election to which rule 40B of Schedule 1 to the 1983
Act applies, and

34.1.b

a local government election, a combined authority mayoral election  , a
combined county authority mayoral election   or a local authority mayoral
election to which the Secretary of State’s duty under section 59A(4) of the
1983 Act applies.

34.2

For the purposes of rule 40B(2) of the elections rules, the presiding officer
must collect the following information—

34.2.a

an indication whether the presiding officer or a clerk explained the voter
identification requirements to each voter prior to the voter making an
