application under rule 37(1) of the elections rules;

34.2.b

the number of voters to whom the presiding officer delivers a ballot paper in
each of the following circumstances—

34.2.b.i

following the production of an anonymous elector’s document by the voter;

34.2.b.ii

following the production of an electoral identity document or a temporary
electoral identity document by the voter;

34.2.c

the number of voters who request the use of a private area of the polling
station for the production of a document in accordance with rule 37(1B) of the
elections rules;

34.2.d

the number of voters to whom the presiding officer refuses to deliver a ballot
paper in accordance with rule 35(3) or 37(1E)(a) or (b) of the elections
rules;

34.2.e

the number of voters to whom the presiding officer, having ascertained the
elector’s name and address following that voter’s application under rule 37 of
the elections rules, is unable to deliver a ballot paper for any of the
following reasons—

34.2.e.i

when asked to produce a specified document, the voter produces a document
other than a specified document;

34.2.e.ii

when asked to produce a specified document, the voter is unable to produce a
specified document;

34.2.f

in respect of each of sub-paragraphs  (d)  and  (e) , the number of such
voters to whom the presiding officer subsequently delivers a ballot paper upon
that person making a further application.

34.3

In paragraph (2)—

34.3.a

a reference to rule 37 of the elections rules includes a reference to that
rule as applied by rule 38, 39 or 40 of the elections rules;

34.3.b

a reference to a presiding officer delivering or refusing to deliver a ballot
paper includes a reference to a presiding officer—

34.3.b.i

causing or refusing to cause a voter’s vote to be marked on a ballot paper in
accordance with paragraph (1) of rule 38 of the elections rules (votes marked
by presiding officer);

34.3.b.ii

granting or refusing an application under paragraph (1) of rule 39 of the
elections rules (voting by persons with disabilities);

34.3.c

a reference to a further application includes a reference to a person seeking
a further time to mark a tendered ballot paper under the paragraph of rule 40
of the elections rules (tendered ballot papers) under which a previous such
attempt was made;

34.3.d

the “ voter identification requirements ” means rule 37(1A) to (1T) of the
elections rules.

#### Collation of information by relevant registration officer or returning officer

35

35.1

Paragraph (2) applies to the information provided to a collating officer—

35.1.a

by each presiding officer in accordance with rule 40B(2)(b) of the elections
rules, or

35.1.b

by the returning officer, in accordance with rule 40B(2)(b) and (3)(a) of the
elections rules.

35.2

For the purposes of rule 40B(5)(b) of the elections rules, the collating
officer must collate the information provided by—

35.2.a

separating that information into two groups depending on whether the
indication by the presiding officer in accordance with regulation  34(2)(a)
is that the explanation described in that regulation was or was not given;

35.2.b

for each group described in sub-paragraph (a), calculating the total number of
voters for each category of information listed in regulation  34(2)(b)  to
(f).

35.3

In this regulation, the “collating officer”—

35.3.a

in relation to an election held in England and Wales is the relevant
registration officer (as defined in rule 40B(12)(b) of the elections rules);

35.3.b

in relation to an election held in Scotland, is the returning officer.

the parliamentary election.

parliamentary election (whether the votes on them have been counted or not)
and it is not necessary to seal up counted and rejected ballot papers in
separate packets.

36.c.20C.65.8

The provisions of these rules as to the inspection, production, retention and
destruction of ballot papers and other documents relating to a poll at a
parliamentary election apply subject to paragraphs (9) and (10).

36.c.20C.65.9

Ballot papers on which the votes were neither counted nor rejected must be
treated as counted ballot papers.

36.c.20C.65.10

No order is to be made for—

36.c.20C.65.10.a

the production or inspection of any ballot papers, or

36.c.20C.65.10.b

the opening of a sealed packet of the completed corresponding number list or
of certificates as to employment on the day of the poll,

unless the order is made by a court with reference to a prosecution.

### Amendment of the Representation of the People (England and Wales) Regulations 2001 and the Representation of the People (Scotland) Regulations 2001

of a proxy for the purposes of voting by proxy at a parliamentary election or

38.4.b.1A.b

A has previously appointed a person (“ B ”) as A’s proxy for those purposes;

38.4.b.1A.c

at the time of making the application, B’s appointment remains in force; and

38.4.b.1A.d

A’s application is made on grounds relating to voter identification which

In regulation 56 (closing date for applications)—

after paragraph (2) insert—

;

;

38.7.d.3D

Where an application is made under paragraph 4(2) or 6(8) of Schedule 4 in
relation to a parliamentary election or a local government election in England
on grounds relating to voter identification, the application must be refused
if it is received after 5pm on the day of the poll at the election for which
it is made.

38.7.d.3E

In paragraphs (2ZA) and (3D), “grounds relating to voter identification” is
interpreted in accordance with regulation 56A(1).

.

38.8

After regulation 56 insert—

########## Grounds relating to voter identification

38.8.56A

38.8.56A.1

For the purposes of this Part, an application is made on grounds relating to
voter identification if it is made because the following apply to B—

38.8.56A.1.a

condition 1, 2, 3 or 4 in this regulation, and

38.8.56A.1.b

except where B has an anonymous entry on the register, condition 5.

38.8.56A.2

In this regulation, “ B ” means—

38.8.56A.2.a

the applicant, where—

38.8.56A.2.a.i

the application is made under paragraph 4(2) of Schedule 4, and

38.8.56A.2.a.ii

regulation 52(1B) does not apply to the application made under paragraph 6(8)
of Schedule 4 which is included in that application under paragraph 4(2);

38.8.56A.2.b

otherwise, the person already appointed as the applicant’s proxy at the time
the application is made.

38.8.56A.3

Condition 1 is that—

38.8.56A.3.a

immediately before the deadline, B has a specified document which B intends to
use to vote in person at a parliamentary election or at a local government
election in England, and

38.8.56A.3.b

after that deadline, that document is—

38.8.56A.3.b.i

lost, stolen, destroyed or damaged so as to be no longer usable as a specified
document for the purposes of that election, or

38.8.56A.3.b.ii

sent by B to another person to prove B’s identity, and B considers it is
unlikely to be returned to B on or before the day of poll at that election.

38.8.56A.4

Condition 2 is that—

38.8.56A.4.a

at a time during the period of 3 months ending with the deadline, B has
applied for a specified document,

38.8.56A.4.b

immediately before the deadline, B has not received that document, and

38.8.56A.4.c

the application for the specified document has not been refused or withdrawn.

38.8.56A.5

Condition 3 is that—

38.8.56A.5.a

B has an anonymous entry on the register, and

38.8.56A.5.b

either—

38.8.56A.5.b.i

B has not been issued with an anonymous elector’s document, or

38.8.56A.5.b.ii

B has been issued with an anonymous elector’s document, and after the deadline
B is allocated an electoral number which is different from the one shown on
that document other than as a result of an application under section 9B of the
1983 Act (anonymous registration).

38.8.56A.6

(6) Condition 4 is that—

38.8.56A.6.a

B has a temporary electoral identity document which is valid for use on the
day of poll at a parliamentary election or a local government election in
England, and

38.8.56A.6.b

before B is able to vote in person at such an election using that document,
proceedings at B’s polling station are adjourned in accordance with rule 42 of
the elections rules (adjournment of poll in case of riot).

38.8.56A.7

Condition 5 is that B does not have access to another specified document.

38.8.56A.8

In this regulation—

38.8.56A.8.a

“anonymous elector’s document” and “temporary electoral identity document”
have the meanings given in regulation  3(1)  of the Voter Identification
Regulations 2022;

38.8.56A.8.b

the “ deadline ” means the time stated in regulation 56(2) or (3) after which,
ignoring any other paragraphs in that regulation, an application under
paragraph 4(2) or 6(7) or (8) of Schedule 4 must be disregarded or refused (as
the case may be) by a registration officer;

38.8.56A.8.c

“ specified document ” has the meaning given in rule 37(1H) and (1K) of the
elections rules.

.

38.9

In regulation 94 (restrictions on supply of full register and disclosure of
information from it by the registration officer and his staff), after
paragraph (4) insert—

38.9.5

In this regulation, references to a registration officer’s registration duties
include references to the officer’s functions under sections 13BD and 13BE of
the 1983 Act.

.

38.10

In regulation 109 (supply of full register etc to police forces and other
agencies), in paragraph (1)(e), at the beginning insert  “in relation to a
register of local government electors in Wales,” .

38.11

In Schedule 3 (forms)—

38.11.a

for Form A (official poll card to be sent to an elector voting in person),
substitute the corresponding form in Part 1 of Schedule 6;

38.11.b

for Form B (official proxy poll card to be sent to an appointed proxy voting
in person), substitute the corresponding form in Part 1 of Schedule 6.

### Amendment of conduct rules for other elections, referendums and recall petitions

#### Amendment of the Local Authorities (Mayoral Elections) (England and Wales) Regulations 2007

42

The Local Authorities (Mayoral Elections) (England and Wales) Regulations 2007
are amended in accordance with regulations  43  to  45 .

#### Amendment of Schedule 1 (mayoral elections rules)

43

43.1

Schedule 1 (mayoral election rules) is amended as follows.

43.2

In the contents list, at the appropriate place—

43.2.a

insert  “41A Refusal to deliver ballot paper: mayoral elections in England” ;

43.2.b

insert  “41B Collection and disclosure of information relating to applications
made under rules 37 to 40 at mayoral elections in England” .

43.3

In rule 2 (interpretation), after paragraph (1) insert—

43.3.1A

(1A) In these Rules, “anonymous elector’s document” and “temporary electoral
identity document” have the meanings given in regulation  3(1)  of the Voter
Identification Regulations 2022.

.

43.4

In rule 25 (provision of polling stations) after paragraph (4) insert—

43.4.5

In the case of a mayoral election held in England, the returning officer must
ensure that each polling station contains an area in which voters can produce
proof of identity in private.

.

43.5

In rule 26 (appointment of presiding officers and polling clerks), in
paragraph (3), at the end insert—

and in respect of a presiding officer for a mayoral election in England only—

43.5.a

refuse to deliver a ballot paper under rule 35(3A) or rule 37(1F) (including
that rule as applied by rules 38, 39 or 40), or

43.5.b

resolve doubts over identity as mentioned in rule 37(1G) (including that rule
as applied by rule 38, 39 or 40).

.

43.6

In rule 28 (equipment of polling stations), before paragraph (6) insert—

43.6.5B

In the case of a mayoral election held in England—

43.6.5B.a

the returning officer must also provide each polling station with a ballot
paper refusal list, in the appropriate form in the Appendix or a form to the
like effect, on which entries are to be made as mentioned in rule 41A (refusal
to deliver ballot paper: mayoral elections in England);

43.6.5B.b

a large notice must be displayed inside each polling station containing—

43.6.5B.b.i

relevant identification details, and

43.6.5B.b.ii

a statement that further proof of identity may be required to resolve any
discrepancy between the name of the holder of a form of identification and the
name of the elector or proxy that the voter claims to be.

43.6.5C

In paragraph (5B)(b)(i), “ relevant identification details ” means details of
the documents the voter needs to produce when applying for a ballot paper,
namely—

43.6.5C.a

in the case of an elector (other than an elector with an anonymous entry) or a
proxy, any of the forms of identification for the time being referred to in
rule 37(1H) of Schedule 1 to the 1983 Act (parliamentary elections rules) ;

43.6.5C.b

in the case of an elector with an anonymous entry, the elector’s official poll
card and an anonymous elector’s document showing the same electoral number as
the electoral number shown on the official poll card.

.

43.7

In rule 35 (questions to be put to voters)—

43.7.a

in the table following paragraph (1), in the column headed “Question”, in
entry 1 (electors), entry 2 (proxies), entry 3 (proxies for an elector with an
anonymous entry), entry 5 (postal voters) and entry 6 (proxy postal voters),
before question (a) insert—

43.7.a.za

At a mayoral election held in England, “What is your name?”

43.7.a.zb

At a mayoral election held in England, “What is your address?”

;

43.7.b

after paragraph (2) insert—

43.7.b.2A

In the case of a mayoral election held in England, where a clerk—

43.7.b.2A.a

gives a person the required information (see paragraph (5)),

43.7.b.2A.b

puts a question specified in paragraph (1) to the person, and

43.7.b.2A.c

decides that the person has failed to answer the question satisfactorily,

the clerk must refer the matter to the presiding officer, who must put the
question to the person again.

;

43.7.c

in paragraph (3), for “A” substitute  “In the case of a mayoral election in
Wales, a” ;

43.7.d

after paragraph (3) insert—

43.7.d.3A

In the case of a mayoral election held in England, where the presiding
officer—

43.7.d.3A.a

gives a person the required information,

43.7.d.3A.b

puts a question specified in paragraph (1) to the person (whether or not
following a referral under paragraph (2A)), and

43.7.d.3A.c

decides that the person has failed to answer the question satisfactorily,

the officer must refuse to deliver a ballot paper to the person (and see rule
41A (procedure where ballot paper is refused under this paragraph)).

43.7.d.3B

For the purposes of this rule, a person answers the question “What is your
name?” or “What is your address?” satisfactorily if—

43.7.d.3B.a

where one of those questions is put, the answer matches a name or address (as
the case may be) in the register of local government electors;

43.7.d.3B.b

where both those questions are put, the answers match a name and address in
that register that relate to the same person.

43.7.d.3C

In the case of an elector in respect of whom a notice has been issued under
section 13B(3B) or (3D) of the 1983 Act, the references to the register in
paragraph (3B) are to be read as references to the notice issued under section
13B(3B) or (3D).

;

43.7.e

in paragraph (4), after “vote” insert  “(and for the purposes of this
paragraph, an inquiry relating to the production of identification by a voter
is not to be regarded as an inquiry as to the right of the person to vote)” ;

43.7.f

after paragraph (4) insert—

43.7.f.5

For the purposes of this rule, a person to whom any question is to be put is
given “the required information” if the person is first informed that—

43.7.f.5.a

a ballot paper will be refused if the person fails to answer each question
satisfactorily, and

43.7.f.5.b

giving false information may be an offence.

.

43.8

In rule 37 (voting procedure)—

43.8.a

in paragraph (1)—

43.8.a.i

for “A” substitute  “Subject to rule 35(3A) and to paragraphs (1A) to (1N), a”
;

43.8.a.ii

in sub-paragraph (a), at the beginning insert  “in the case of a mayoral
election in Wales only,” ;

43.8.b

after paragraph (1) insert—

43.8.b.1A

Paragraphs (1B) to (1N) apply in the case of a mayoral election held in
England.

43.8.b.1B

A ballot paper must not be delivered to a voter unless the voter produces a
specified document to the presiding officer or a clerk.

43.8.b.1C

The presiding officer or clerk must arrange for the voter to produce any
document in a private area of the polling station if the voter so requests,
and, in such a case, must ensure that no other persons witness the production
except as permitted by the voter.

43.8.b.1D

Paragraph (1E) applies in relation to a voter where—

43.8.b.1D.a

the voter produces a specified document to a clerk and the clerk decides that
the document raises a reasonable doubt as to whether the voter is the elector
or proxy that the voter claims to be, or

43.8.b.1D.b

the voter produces a document to a clerk that the clerk reasonably suspects to
be a forged document.

43.8.b.1E

Where this paragraph applies, the clerk must refer the matter and produce the
document to the presiding officer, who must proceed as if the voter had
produced the document to the presiding officer in the first place.

43.8.b.1F

The presiding officer must refuse to deliver a ballot paper to a voter where—

43.8.b.1F.a

the voter produces a specified document to the officer and the officer decides
that the document raises a reasonable doubt as to whether the voter is the
elector or proxy that the voter claims to be, or

43.8.b.1F.b

the voter produces a document to the officer that the officer reasonably
suspects to be a forged document.

43.8.b.1G

Paragraph (1F)(a) does not apply where—

43.8.b.1G.a

a discrepancy between the name of the holder of a specified document and the
name of the elector or proxy that the voter claims to be is resolved to the
presiding officer’s satisfaction at the time of the application by the voter
producing further proof of identity, and

43.8.b.1G.b

the presiding officer has no other reason (arising from any document produced
by the voter) to doubt that the voter is the elector or proxy that the voter
claims to be.

43.8.b.1H

The refusal to deliver a ballot paper to a voter under paragraph (1F) does not
prevent the voter making a further application under paragraph (1), and
paragraphs (1B) to (1G) apply on any further application.

43.8.b.1I

In this rule, a “ forged document ” means a false document made to resemble a
specified document.

43.8.b.1J

In this rule, a “specified document”—

43.8.b.1J.a

except in the case of a voter who has an anonymous entry in the register of
electors, means a document which for the time being falls within the list
specified in rule 37(1H) of Schedule 1 to the 1983 Act (parliamentary
elections rules);

43.8.b.1J.b

in the case of a voter who has an anonymous entry in the register of electors,
means an anonymous elector’s document which—

43.8.b.1J.b.i

was issued by the registration officer for the local authority in whose area
the election is held, and

43.8.b.1J.b.ii

contains the number—

43.8.b.1J.b.ii.aa

allocated to the voter as stated in the copy of the register of electors, or

43.8.b.1J.b.ii.bb

where an entry relating to the voter is added to the register in pursuance of
a notice issued under section 13B(3B) or (3D) of the 1983 Act, as stated in
the copy of that notice.

43.8.b.1K

Subject to paragraph (1L), a reference in this rule to a document that is a
specified document is a reference to the document regardless of any expiry
date relating to it.

43.8.b.1L

Paragraph (1K) does not apply to a temporary electoral identity document where
the date of the poll for the election is after the date for which the document
is issued.

43.8.b.1M

No person other than the presiding officer or a clerk may inspect a document
produced as proof of a voter’s identity, except as permitted by the voter.

43.8.b.1N

References in this rule to producing a document are to producing it for
inspection.

;

43.8.c

in paragraph (2), after “elector” insert  “in respect of a mayoral election in
Wales” .

43.9

In rule 38 (votes marked by presiding officer)—

43.9.a

in paragraph (1), for “The” substitute  “Subject to paragraph (1A), the” ;

43.9.b

after paragraph (1) insert—

43.9.b.1A

Paragraphs (1B) to (1N) of rule 37 apply in the case of a voter at a mayoral
election held in England who applies under paragraph (1) of this rule as those
paragraphs apply in the case of a voter who applies under rule 37(1), but as
if—

43.9.b.1A.a

references to delivering a ballot paper to a voter were to causing a voter’s
vote to be marked on a ballot paper, and

43.9.b.1A.b

in rule 37(1H), the reference to paragraph (1) of rule 37 were to paragraph
(1) of this rule.

.

43.10

In rule 39 (voting by persons with disabilities)—

43.10.a

in paragraph (2), for “If” substitute  “Subject to paragraph (2A), if” ;

43.10.b

after paragraph (2) insert—

43.10.b.2A

Paragraphs (1B) to (1N) of rule 37 apply in the case of a voter at a mayoral
election held in England who applies under paragraph (1) of this rule as those
paragraphs apply in the case of a voter who applies under rule 37(1), but as
if—

43.10.b.2A.a

references to delivering a ballot paper to a voter were to granting a voter’s
application, and

43.10.b.2A.b

in rule 37(1H), the reference to paragraph (1) of rule 37 were to paragraph
(1) of this rule.

.

43.11

In rule 40 (tendered ballot papers – circumstances where available), after
paragraph (6) insert—

43.11.7

Paragraphs (1B) to (1N) of rule 37 apply in the case of a person who seeks to
mark a tendered ballot paper under this rule at a mayoral election held in
England as they apply in the case of a voter who applies for a ballot paper
under rule 37(1), but as if, in rule 37(1H) the reference to making a further
application under paragraph (1) of rule 37 were to seeking a further time to
mark a tendered ballot paper under the paragraph of this rule under which the
first such attempt was made.

.

43.12

After rule 41 (tendered ballot papers – general provisions) insert—

########## Refusal to deliver ballot paper: mayoral elections in England

43.12.41A

43.12.41A.1

This rule applies in relation to a mayoral election held in England.

43.12.41A.2

Where a presiding officer refuses to deliver a ballot paper to a voter who
applied for one as an elector, the officer or a clerk must enter on the ballot
paper refusal list—

43.12.41A.2.a

the voter’s electoral number, and

43.12.41A.2.b

against that number, the reason for the refusal.

43.12.41A.3

Where a presiding officer refuses to deliver a ballot paper to a voter who
applied for one as a proxy, the officer or a clerk must enter on the ballot
paper refusal list—

43.12.41A.3.a

the name and address of the voter, and

43.12.41A.3.b

against those details, the reason for the refusal.

43.12.41A.4

Paragraphs (5) and (6) apply where—

43.12.41A.4.a

a presiding officer refuses to deliver a ballot paper to a voter under rule
37(1F), and

43.12.41A.4.b

the voter makes a further application as permitted by rule 37(1H).

43.12.41A.5

If a ballot paper is delivered to the voter following that application, the
presiding officer or a clerk must note that fact on the ballot paper refusal
list.

43.12.41A.6

If the presiding officer again refuses to deliver a ballot paper to the voter,
the presiding officer or a clerk must note that fact on the ballot paper
refusal list.

43.12.41A.7

Entries required by this rule to be made on the ballot paper refusal list must
be made as soon as practicable after delivery of a ballot paper to a voter is
refused (or, in the case mentioned in paragraph (5), as soon as practicable
after the delivery of a ballot paper to a voter).

43.12.41A.8

For the purposes of paragraph (2)(a), a person’s “electoral number” is the
number—

43.12.41A.8.a

allocated to the person as stated in the copy of the register of electors, or

43.12.41A.8.b

where an entry relating to the person is added to the register in pursuance of
a notice issued under section 13B(3B) or (3D) of the 1983 Act, as stated in
the copy of that notice.

43.12.41A.9

Subject to rule 37(1H) and paragraph (10), a refusal to deliver a ballot paper
to a voter is final and may not be questioned in any proceeding whatsoever.

43.12.41A.10

A refusal to deliver a ballot paper to a voter is subject to review on an
election petition.

43.12.41A.11

In this rule—

43.12.41A.11.a

except in paragraph (4)(a), any reference to the refusal to deliver a ballot
paper (however expressed) is to the refusal to do so under rule 35(3A) or
37(1F), and

43.12.41A.11.b

any reference to paragraph (1F) or (1H) of rule 37 includes a reference to
that paragraph as applied by rule 38, 39 or 40.

########## Collection and disclosure of information relating to applications made under rules 37 to 40 at mayoral elections in England

43.12.41B

43.12.41B.1

This rule applies in relation to a mayoral election to which the Secretary of
State’s duty under section 59A(4) of the 1983 Act (reports on voter
identification requirements in respect of local government elections) applies
by virtue of subsection (5A) of that section.

43.12.41B.2

The presiding officer must—

43.12.41B.2.a

collect the information described in regulation  34  of the Voter
Identification Regulations 2022 (collection of information by presiding
officer) relating to applications made under rules 37(1), 38(1), 39(1) or
40(1), and

43.12.41B.2.b

provide that information to the returning officer as soon as practicable after
the close of the poll.

43.12.41B.3

The returning officer must forward the information to the relevant
registration officer.

43.12.41B.4

As soon as reasonably practicable after receiving the information the relevant
registration officer must—

43.12.41B.4.a

anonymise the information by removing from it all names and electoral numbers
of the people to whom the information relates, and

43.12.41B.4.b

collate the information in accordance with regulation  35  of the Voter
Identification Regulations 2022 (collation of information by relevant
registration officer).

The information as anonymised and collated in accordance with this paragraph
is referred to in the rest of this rule as “the paragraph (4) information”.

43.12.41B.5

The relevant registration officer must provide the paragraph (4) information—

43.12.41B.5.a

to the Secretary of State, as soon as reasonably practicable after taking the
steps required by paragraph (4), and

43.12.41B.5.b

where they request the information, to the Electoral Commission.

43.12.41B.6

The relevant registration officer must not disclose the paragraph (4)
information otherwise than in accordance with paragraph (5).

43.12.41B.7

The relevant registration officer must retain the information anonymised in
accordance with paragraph (4)(a) for at least 10 years.

43.12.41B.8

For the purpose of paragraph (4)(a), a person’s “electoral number” is the
number—

43.12.41B.8.a

allocated to the person as stated in the copy of the register of electors, or

43.12.41B.8.b

where an entry relating to the person is added to the register in pursuance of
a notice issued under section 13B(3B) or (3D) of the 1983 Act, as stated in
the copy of that notice.

43.12.41B.9

Except as provided by paragraph (10), a disclosure of information under this
rule does not breach—

43.12.41B.9.a

any obligation of confidence owed by the presiding officer, the returning
officer or a registration officer, or

43.12.41B.9.b

any other restriction on the disclosure of information (however imposed).

43.12.41B.10

Nothing in this rule authorises the making of a disclosure that contravenes
the data protection legislation (but in determining whether a disclosure would
do so, the duties imposed by paragraphs (2) and (3) are to be taken into
account).

43.12.41B.11

In this rule—

43.12.41B.11.a

“ the data protection legislation ” has the same meaning as in the Data
Protection Act 2018 ;

43.12.41B.11.b

references to the relevant registration officer are to the registration
officer of the local authority in whose area the election is held.

.

43.13

In rule 45 (procedure on close of poll), in paragraph (1) after sub-paragraph
(d) insert—

43.13.da

in the case of a mayoral election held in England, the ballot paper refusal
list completed in accordance with rule 41A,

.

43.14

In rule 56 (sealing up of ballot papers), in paragraph (2) after sub-paragraph
(a) insert—

43.14.aa

in the case of a mayoral election held in England, the completed ballot paper
refusal list,

.

43.15

In rule 58 (orders for production of documents), after paragraph (1) insert—

43.15.1A

An order—

43.15.1A.a

for the opening of the sealed packet containing a completed ballot paper
refusal list, or

43.15.1A.b

for the inspection or production of that list,

may be made by the county court if satisfied by evidence on oath that the
order is required for the purpose of an election petition relating to a
mayoral election held in England.

.

(for use at mayoral elections in England)” ;

45.8

in paragraph (1)—

for “A” substitute  “Subject to rule 35(3A) and to paragraphs (1A) to (1N), a”

45.8.a.ii

45.8.b

after paragraph (1) insert—

45.8.b.1A

Paragraphs (1B) to (1N) apply in the case of a mayoral election held in
England.

45.8.b.1B

A ballot paper must not be delivered to a voter unless the voter produces a
specified document to the presiding officer or a clerk.

45.8.b.1C

The presiding officer or clerk must arrange for the voter to produce any
document in a private area of the polling station if the voter so requests,
and, in such a case, must ensure that no other persons witness the production
except as permitted by the voter.

45.8.b.1D

Paragraph (1E) applies in relation to a voter where—

45.8.b.1D.a

the voter produces a specified document to a clerk and the clerk decides that
the document raises a reasonable doubt as to whether the voter is the elector
or proxy that the voter claims to be, or

45.8.b.1D.b

the voter produces a document to a clerk that the clerk reasonably suspects to
be a forged document.

45.8.b.1E

Where this paragraph applies, the clerk must refer the matter and produce the
document to the presiding officer, who must proceed as if the voter had
produced the document to the presiding officer in the first place.

45.8.b.1F

The presiding officer must refuse to deliver a ballot paper to a voter where—

45.8.b.1F.a

the voter produces a specified document to the officer and the officer decides
that the document raises a reasonable doubt as to whether the voter is the
elector or proxy that the voter claims to be, or

45.8.b.1F.b

the voter produces a document to the officer that the officer reasonably
suspects to be a forged document.

45.8.b.1G

Paragraph (1F)(a) does not apply where—

45.8.b.1G.a

a discrepancy between the name of the holder of a specified document and the
name of the elector or proxy that the voter claims to be is resolved to the
presiding officer’s satisfaction at the time of the application by the voter
producing further proof of identity, and

45.8.b.1G.b

the presiding officer has no other reason (arising from any document produced
by the voter) to doubt that the voter is the elector or proxy that the voter
claims to be.

45.8.b.1H

The refusal to deliver a ballot paper to a voter under paragraph (1F) does not
prevent the voter making a further application under paragraph (1), and
paragraphs (1B) to (1G) apply on any further application.

45.8.b.1I

In this rule, a “ forged document ” means a false document made to resemble a
specified document.

45.8.b.1J

In this rule, a “specified document”—

45.8.b.1J.a

except in the case of a voter who has an anonymous entry in the register of
electors, means a document which for the time being falls within the list
specified in rule 37(1H) of Schedule 1 to the 1983 Act (parliamentary
elections rules);

45.8.b.1J.b

in the case of a voter who has an anonymous entry in the register of electors,
means an anonymous elector’s document which—

45.8.b.1J.b.i

was issued by the registration officer for the local authority in whose area
the election is held, and

45.8.b.1J.b.ii

contains the number—

45.8.b.1J.b.ii.aa

allocated to the voter as stated in the copy of the register of electors, or

45.8.b.1J.b.ii.bb

where an entry relating to the voter is added to the register in pursuance of
a notice issued under section 13B(3B) or (3D) of the 1983 Act, as stated in
the copy of that notice.

45.8.b.1K

Subject to paragraph (1L), a reference in this rule to a document that is a
specified document is a reference to the document regardless of any expiry
date relating to it.

45.8.b.1L

Paragraph (1K) does not apply to a temporary electoral identity document where
the date of the poll for the election is after the date for which the document
is issued.

45.8.b.1M

No person other than the presiding officer or a clerk may inspect a document
produced as proof of a voter’s identity, except as permitted by the voter.

45.8.b.1N

References in this rule to producing a document are to producing it for
inspection.

;

45.8.c

in paragraph (2), after “elector” insert  “in respect of a mayoral election in
Wales” .

45.9

In rule 38 (votes marked by presiding officer)—

45.9.b.1A

Paragraphs (1B) to (1N) of rule 37 apply in the case of a voter at a mayoral
election held in England who applies under paragraph (1) of this rule as those
paragraphs apply in the case of a voter who applies under rule 37(1), but as
if—

45.9.b.1A.a

references to delivering a ballot paper to a voter were to causing a voter’s
vote to be marked on a ballot paper, and

under rule 37(1), but as if, in rule 37(1H) the reference to making a further

.

45.12

After rule 41 (tendered ballot papers – general provisions) insert—

########## Refusal to deliver ballot paper: mayoral elections in England

45.12.41A

45.12.41A.1

This rule applies in relation to a mayoral election held in England.

45.12.41A.2

Where a presiding officer refuses to deliver a ballot paper to a voter who
applied for one as an elector, the officer or a clerk must enter on the ballot
paper refusal list—

45.12.41A.2.a

the voter’s electoral number, and

45.12.41A.2.b

against that number, the reason for the refusal.

45.12.41A.3

Where a presiding officer refuses to deliver a ballot paper to a voter who
applied for one as a proxy, the officer or a clerk must enter on the ballot
paper refusal list—

45.12.41A.3.a

the name and address of the voter, and

45.12.41A.3.b

against those details, the reason for the refusal.

45.12.41A.4

Paragraphs (5) and (6) apply where—

45.12.41A.4.a

a presiding officer refuses to deliver a ballot paper to a voter under rule
37(1F), and

45.12.41A.4.b

the voter makes a further application as permitted by rule 37(1H).

45.12.41A.5

If a ballot paper is delivered to the voter following that application, the
presiding officer or a clerk must note that fact on the ballot paper refusal
list.

45.12.41A.6

If the presiding officer again refuses to deliver a ballot paper to the voter,
the presiding officer or a clerk must note that fact on the ballot paper
refusal list.

45.12.41A.7

Entries required by this rule to be made on the ballot paper refusal list must
be made as soon as practicable after delivery of a ballot paper to a voter is
refused (or, in the case mentioned in paragraph (5), as soon as practicable
after the delivery of a ballot paper to a voter).

45.12.41A.8

For the purposes of paragraph (2)(a), a person’s “electoral number” is the
number—

45.12.41A.8.a

allocated to the person as stated in the copy of the register of electors, or

45.12.41A.8.b

where an entry relating to the person is added to the register in pursuance of
a notice issued under section 13B(3B) or (3D) of the 1983 Act, as stated in
the copy of that notice.

45.12.41A.9

Subject to rule 37(1H) and paragraph (10), a refusal to deliver a ballot paper
to a voter is final and may not be questioned in any proceeding whatsoever.

45.12.41A.10

A refusal to deliver a ballot paper to a voter is subject to review on an
election petition.

45.12.41A.11

In this rule—

45.12.41A.11.a

except in paragraph (4)(a), any reference to the refusal to deliver a ballot
paper (however expressed) is to the refusal to do so under rule 35(3A) or
37(1F), and

45.12.41A.11.b

any reference to paragraph (1F) or (1H) of rule 37 includes a reference to
that paragraph as applied by rule 38, 39 or 40.

########## Collection and disclosure of information relating to applications made under rules 37 to 40 at mayoral elections in England

45.12.41B

45.12.41B.1

This rule applies in relation to a mayoral election to which the Secretary of
State’s duty under section 59A(4) of the 1983 Act (reports on voter
identification requirements in respect of local government elections) applies
by virtue of subsection (5A) of that section.

45.12.41B.2

The presiding officer must—

45.12.41B.2.a

collect the information described in regulation  34  of the Voter
Identification Regulations 2022 (collection of information by presiding
officer) relating to applications made under rules 37(1), 38(1), 39(1) or
40(1), and

45.12.41B.2.b

provide that information to the returning officer as soon as practicable after
the close of the poll.

45.12.41B.3

The returning officer must forward the information to the relevant
registration officer.

45.12.41B.4

As soon as reasonably practicable after receiving the information the relevant
registration officer must—

45.12.41B.4.a

anonymise the information by removing from it all names and electoral numbers
of the people to whom the information relates, and

45.12.41B.4.b

collate the information in accordance with regulation  35  of the Voter
Identification Regulations 2022 (collation of information by relevant
registration officer).

The information as anonymised and collated in accordance with this paragraph
is referred to in the rest of this rule as “the paragraph (4) information”.

45.12.41B.5

The relevant registration officer must provide the paragraph (4) information—

45.12.41B.5.a

to the Secretary of State, as soon as reasonably practicable after taking the
steps required by paragraph (4), and

45.12.41B.5.b

where they request the information, to the Electoral Commission.

45.12.41B.6

The relevant registration officer must not disclose the paragraph (4)
information otherwise than in accordance with paragraph (5).

45.12.41B.7

The relevant registration officer must retain the information anonymised in
accordance with paragraph (4)(a) for at least 10 years.

45.12.41B.8

For the purpose of paragraph (4)(a), a person’s “electoral number” is the
number—

45.12.41B.8.a

allocated to the person as stated in the copy of the register of electors, or

45.12.41B.8.b

where an entry relating to the person is added to the register in pursuance of
a notice issued under section 13B(3B) or (3D) of the 1983 Act, as stated in
the copy of that notice.

45.12.41B.9

Except as provided by paragraph (10), a disclosure of information under this
rule does not breach—

45.12.41B.9.a

any obligation of confidence owed by the presiding officer, the returning
officer or a registration officer, or

45.12.41B.9.b

any other restriction on the disclosure of information (however imposed).

45.12.41B.10

Nothing in this rule authorises the making of a disclosure that contravenes
the data protection legislation (but in determining whether a disclosure would
do so, the duties imposed by paragraphs (2) and (3) are to be taken into
account).

45.12.41B.11

In this rule—

45.12.41B.11.a

“ the data protection legislation ” has the same meaning as in the Data
Protection Act 2018;

45.12.41B.11.b

references to the relevant registration officer are to the registration
officer of the local authority in whose area the election is held.

.

45.13

In rule 45 (procedure on close of poll), in paragraph (1) after sub-paragraph
(d) insert—

45.13.da

in the case of a mayoral election held in England, the ballot paper refusal
list completed in accordance with rule 41A,

.

45.14

(a) insert—

45.14.aa

in the case of a mayoral election held in England, the completed ballot paper
refusal list, or

.

45.15

In rule 58 (orders for production of documents), after paragraph (1) insert—

45.15.1A

An order—

45.15.1A.a

for the opening of the sealed packet containing a completed ballot paper
refusal list, or

45.15.1A.b

for the inspection or production of that list,

may be made by the county court if satisfied by evidence on oath that the
order is required for the purpose of an election petition relating to a
mayoral election held in England.

.

48.7

In rule 24 (questions to be put to voters and proxies)—

48.7.a

48.7.a.za

What is your name?

48.7.a.zb

What is your address?

;

48.7.b

after paragraph (2) insert—

48.7.b.2A

Where a clerk—

48.7.b.2A.a

gives a person the required information (see paragraph (5)),

48.7.b.2A.b

puts a question specified in paragraph (1) to the person, and

48.7.b.2A.c

decides that the person has failed to answer the question satisfactorily,

the clerk must refer the matter to the presiding officer, who must put the
question to the person again.

;

48.7.c

for paragraph (3) substitute—

48.7.c.3

Where the presiding officer—

48.7.c.3.a

gives the person the required information,

48.7.c.3.b

puts a question specified in paragraph (1) to the person (whether or not
following a referral under paragraph (2A)), and

48.7.c.3.c

decides that the person has failed to answer the question satisfactorily,

the officer must refuse to deliver a ballot paper to the person (and see rule
30A for the procedure where a ballot paper is refused under this paragraph).

48.7.c.3A

For the purposes of this rule, a person answers the question “What is your
name?” or “What is your address?” satisfactorily if—

48.7.c.3A.a

where one of those questions is put, the answer matches a name or address (as
the case may be) in the register of electors;

48.7.c.3A.b

where both those questions are put, the answers match a name and address in
that register that relate to the same person.

48.7.c.3B

In the case of a person in respect of whom a notice has been issued under
section 13B(3B) or (3D) of the 1983 Act, the references to the register in
paragraph (3A) are to be read as references to the notice issued under section
13B(3B) or (3D).

;

48.7.d

in paragraph (4), after “vote” insert  “(and for the purposes of this
paragraph, an inquiry relating to the production of identification by a person
is not to be regarded as an inquiry as to the right of the person to vote)” ;

48.7.e

after paragraph (4) insert—

48.7.e.5

For the purposes of this rule, a person to whom any question is to be put is
given “the required information” if the person is first informed that—

48.7.e.5.a

a ballot paper will be refused if the person fails to answer each question
satisfactorily, and

48.7.e.5.b

giving false information may be an offence.

.

48.8

In rule 26 (voting procedure)—

48.8.a

in paragraph (1)—

48.8.a.i

for “A” substitute  “Subject to rule 24(3) and to paragraphs (1A) to (1M), a”
;

48.8.a.ii

omit sub-paragraph (a);

48.8.b

after paragraph (1) insert—

48.8.b.1A

A ballot paper must not be delivered to a voter or proxy unless the voter or
proxy produces a specified document to the presiding officer or a clerk.

48.8.b.1B

The presiding officer or clerk must arrange for the voter or proxy to produce
any document in a private area of the polling station if the voter or proxy so
requests, and, in such a case, must ensure that no other persons witness the
production except as permitted by the voter or proxy.

48.8.b.1C

Paragraph (1D) applies in relation to a voter or proxy where—

48.8.b.1C.a

the voter or proxy produces a specified document to a clerk and the clerk
decides that the document raises a reasonable doubt as to whether the voter or
proxy is the voter or proxy that the voter or proxy claims to be, or

48.8.b.1C.b

the voter or proxy produces a document to a clerk that the clerk reasonably
suspects to be a forged document.

48.8.b.1D

Where this paragraph applies, the clerk must refer the matter and produce the
document to the presiding officer, who must proceed as if the voter or proxy
had produced the document to the presiding officer in the first place.

48.8.b.1E

The presiding officer must refuse to deliver a ballot paper to a voter or
proxy where—

48.8.b.1E.a

the voter or proxy produces a specified document to the officer and the
officer decides that the document raises a reasonable doubt as to whether the
voter or proxy is the voter or proxy that the voter or proxy claims to be, or

48.8.b.1E.b

the voter or proxy produces a document to the officer that the officer
reasonably suspects to be a forged document.

48.8.b.1F

Paragraph (1E)(a) does not apply where—

48.8.b.1F.a

a discrepancy between the name of the holder of a specified document and the
name of the voter or proxy that the voter or proxy claims to be is resolved to
the presiding officer’s satisfaction at the time of the application by the
voter or proxy producing further proof of identity, and

48.8.b.1F.b

the presiding officer has no other reason (arising from any document produced
by the voter or proxy) to doubt that the voter or proxy is the voter or proxy
that the voter or proxy claims to be.

48.8.b.1G

The refusal to deliver a ballot paper to a voter or proxy under paragraph (1E)
does not prevent the voter or proxy making a further application under
paragraph (1), and paragraphs (1A) to (1F) apply on any further application.

48.8.b.1H

In this rule, a “ forged document ” means a false document made to resemble a
specified document.

48.8.b.1I

In this rule, a “specified document”—

48.8.b.1I.a

except in the case of a voter or proxy who has an anonymous entry in the
register of electors, is one which for the time being falls within the list
specified in rule 37(1H) of Schedule 1 to the 1983 Act (parliamentary election
rules);

48.8.b.1I.b

in the case of a voter or proxy who has an anonymous entry in the register of
electors, means an anonymous elector’s document which—

48.8.b.1I.b.i

was issued by the registration officer for the local authority in whose area
the referendum is held, and

48.8.b.1I.b.ii

contains the number—

48.8.b.1I.b.ii.aa

allocated to the voter or proxy as stated in the copy of the register of
electors, or

48.8.b.1I.b.ii.bb

where an entry relating to the voter or proxy is added to the register in
pursuance of a notice issued under section 13B(3B) or (3D) of the 1983 Act, as
stated in the copy of that notice.

48.8.b.1J

Subject to paragraph (1K), a reference in this rule to a document that is a
specified document is a reference to the document regardless of any expiry
date relating to it.

48.8.b.1K

Paragraph (1J) does not apply to a temporary electoral identity document where
the date of the poll for the referendum is after the date for which the
document is issued.

48.8.b.1L

No person other than the presiding officer or a clerk may inspect a document
produced as proof of a voter’s or proxy’s identity, except as permitted by the
voter or proxy.

48.8.b.1M

References in this rule to producing a document are to producing it for
inspection.

;

48.8.c

in paragraph (2), omit the words from “and only” to the end;

48.8.d

omit paragraph (3)(a).

########## Refusal to deliver ballot paper

48.12.30A

48.12.30A.1

Where a presiding officer refuses to deliver a ballot paper to a voter who
applied for one other than as a proxy, the officer or a clerk must enter on
the ballot paper refusal list—

48.12.30A.1.a

the voter’s electoral number, and

48.12.30A.1.b

against that number, the reason for the refusal.

48.12.30A.2

Where a presiding officer refuses to deliver a ballot paper to a voter who
applied for one as a proxy, the officer or a clerk must enter on the ballot
paper refusal list—

48.12.30A.2.a

the name and address of the voter, and

48.12.30A.2.b

against those details, the reason for the refusal.

48.12.30A.3

Paragraphs (4) and (5) apply where—

48.12.30A.3.a

a presiding officer refuses to deliver a ballot paper to a voter or proxy
under rule 26(1E), and

48.12.30A.3.b

the voter or proxy makes a further application under rule 26(1).

48.12.30A.4

If a ballot paper is delivered to the voter or proxy following a further
application, the presiding officer or a clerk must note that fact on the
ballot paper refusal list.

48.12.30A.5

If the presiding officer again refuses to deliver a ballot paper to the voter
or proxy, the presiding officer or a clerk must note that fact on the ballot
paper refusal list.

48.12.30A.6

Entries required by this rule to be made on the ballot paper refusal list must
be made as soon as practicable after delivery of a ballot paper to a voter or
proxy is refused (or, in the case mentioned in paragraph (4), as soon as
practicable after the delivery of a ballot paper to a voter or proxy).

48.12.30A.7

For the purposes of paragraph (1)(a), a person’s “electoral number” is the
number—

48.12.30A.7.a

allocated to the person as stated in the copy of the register of electors, or

48.12.30A.7.b

where an entry relating to the person is added to the register in pursuance of
a notice issued under section 13B(3B) or (3D) of the 1983 Act, as stated in
the copy of that notice.

48.12.30A.8

Subject to rule 26(1G) and paragraph (9), a refusal to deliver a ballot paper
to a voter or proxy is final and may not be questioned in any proceeding
whatsoever.

48.12.30A.9

A refusal to deliver a ballot paper to a voter or proxy is subject to review
on a referendum petition.

48.12.30A.10

In this rule—

48.12.30A.10.a

except in paragraph (3)(a), any reference to the refusal to deliver a ballot
paper (however expressed) is to the refusal to do so under rule 24(3) or
26(1E), and

48.12.30A.10.b

any reference to paragraph (1E) or (1G) of rule 26 includes a reference to
that paragraph as applied by rule 27, 28 or 29.

.

50.6.b.8A

A large notice must be displayed inside each polling station containing—

50.6.b.8A.a

details of the documents the voter or proxy needs to produce when applying for

50.6.b.8A.a.i

in the case of a voter (other than a voter with an anonymous entry) or a

50.6.b.8A.a.ii

50.7

In rule 26 (questions to be put to voters and proxies)—

50.7.a

in the table following paragraph (1), in the column headed “Questions”, in
entry 1 (voters), entry 2 (proxies), entry 3 (proxies for a voter with an
anonymous entry), entry 5 (postal voters) and entry 6 (proxy postal voters),
before question (a) insert—

50.7.a.za

What is your name?

50.7.a.zb

What is your address?

;

50.7.b

after paragraph (2) insert—

50.7.b.2A

Where a clerk—

50.7.b.2A.a

gives a person the required information (see paragraph (5)),

50.7.b.2A.b

puts a question specified in paragraph (1) to the person, and

50.7.b.2A.c

decides that the person has failed to answer the question satisfactorily,

the clerk must refer the matter to the presiding officer, who must put the
question to the person again.

;

50.7.c

for paragraph (3) substitute—

50.7.c.3

Where the presiding officer—

50.7.c.3.a

gives the person the required information,

50.7.c.3.b

puts a question specified in paragraph (1) to the person (whether or not
following a referral under paragraph (2A)), and

50.7.c.3.c

decides that the person has failed to answer the question satisfactorily,

the officer must refuse to deliver a ballot paper to the person (and see rule
32A for the procedure where a ballot paper is refused under this paragraph).

50.7.c.3A

For the purposes of this rule, a person answers the question “What is your
name?” or “What is your address?” satisfactorily if—

50.7.c.3A.a

where one of those questions is put, the answer matches a name or address (as
the case may be) in the register of electors;

50.7.c.3A.b

where both those questions are put, the answers match a name and address in
that register that relate to the same person.

50.7.c.3B

In the case of a person in respect of whom a notice has been issued under
section 13B(3B) or (3D) of the 1983 Act, the references to the register in
paragraph (3A) are to be read as references to the notice issued under section
13B(3B) or (3D).

;

50.7.d

in paragraph (4), after “vote” insert  “(and for the purposes of this
paragraph, an inquiry relating to the production of identification by a person
is not to be regarded as an inquiry as to the right of the person to vote)” ;

50.7.e

after paragraph (4) insert—

50.7.e.5

For the purposes of this rule, a person to whom any question is to be put is
given “the required information” if the person is first informed that—

50.7.e.5.a

a ballot paper will be refused if the person fails to answer each question
satisfactorily, and

50.7.e.5.b

giving false information may be an offence.

.

50.8

In rule 28 (voting procedure)—

50.8.a

in paragraph (1)—

50.8.a.i

for “A” substitute  “Subject to rule 26(3) and to paragraphs (1A) to (1M), a”
;

50.8.a.ii

omit sub-paragraph (a);

50.8.b

after paragraph (1) insert—

50.8.b.1A

A ballot paper must not be delivered to a voter or proxy unless the voter or
proxy produces a specified document to the presiding officer or a clerk.

50.8.b.1B

The presiding officer or clerk must arrange for the voter or proxy to produce
any document in a private area of the polling station if the voter or proxy so
requests, and, in such a case, must ensure that no other persons witness the
production except as permitted by the voter or proxy.

50.8.b.1C

Paragraph (1D) applies in relation to a voter or proxy where—

50.8.b.1C.a

the voter or proxy produces a specified document to a clerk and the clerk
decides that the document raises a reasonable doubt as to whether the voter or
proxy is the voter or proxy that the voter or proxy claims to be, or

50.8.b.1C.b

the voter or proxy produces a document to a clerk that the clerk reasonably
suspects to be a forged document.

50.8.b.1D

Where this paragraph applies, the clerk must refer the matter and produce the
document to the presiding officer, who must proceed as if the voter or proxy
had produced the document to the presiding officer in the first place.

50.8.b.1E

The presiding officer must refuse to deliver a ballot paper to a voter or
proxy where—

50.8.b.1E.a

the voter or proxy produces a specified document to the officer and the
officer decides that the document raises a reasonable doubt as to whether the
voter or proxy is the voter or proxy that the voter or proxy claims to be, or

50.8.b.1E.b

the voter or proxy produces a document to the officer that the officer
reasonably suspects to be a forged document.

50.8.b.1F

Paragraph (1E)(a) does not apply where—

50.8.b.1F.a

a discrepancy between the name of the holder of a specified document and the
name of the voter or proxy that the voter or proxy claims to be is resolved to
the presiding officer’s satisfaction at the time of the application by the
voter or proxy producing further proof of identity, and

50.8.b.1F.b

the presiding officer has no other reason (arising from any document produced
by the voter or proxy) to doubt that the voter or proxy is the voter or proxy
that the voter or proxy claims to be.

50.8.b.1G

The refusal to deliver a ballot paper to a voter or proxy under paragraph (1E)
does not prevent the voter or proxy making a further application under
paragraph (1), and paragraphs (1A) to (1F) apply on any further application.

50.8.b.1H

In this rule, a “ forged document ” means a false document made to resemble a
specified document.

50.8.b.1I

In this rule, a “specified document”—

50.8.b.1I.a

except in the case of a voter or proxy who has an anonymous entry in the
register of electors, is one which for the time being falls within the list
specified in rule 37(1H) of Schedule 1 to the 1983 Act (parliamentary election
rules);

50.8.b.1I.b

in the case of a voter or proxy who has an anonymous entry in the register of
electors, means an anonymous elector’s document which—

50.8.b.1I.b.i

was issued by the registration officer for the local authority in whose area
the referendum is held, and

50.8.b.1I.b.ii

contains the number—

50.8.b.1I.b.ii.aa

allocated to the voter or proxy as stated in the copy of the register of
electors, or

50.8.b.1I.b.ii.bb

where an entry relating to the voter or proxy is added to the register in
pursuance of a notice issued under section 13B(3B) or (3D) of the 1983 Act, as
stated in the copy of that notice.

50.8.b.1J

Subject to paragraph (1K), a reference in this rule to a document that is a
specified document is a reference to the document regardless of any expiry
date relating to it.

50.8.b.1K

Paragraph (1J) does not apply to a temporary electoral identity document where
the date of the poll for the referendum is after the date for which the
document is issued.

50.8.b.1L

No person other than the presiding officer or a clerk may inspect a document
produced as proof of a voter’s or proxy’s identity, except as permitted by the
voter or proxy.

50.8.b.1M

References in this rule to producing a document are to producing it for
inspection.

;

50.8.c

in paragraph (2), omit the words from “and only” to the end;

50.8.d

omit paragraph (3)(a).

50.9

In rule 29 (votes marked by the presiding officer)—

50.9.a

in paragraph (1), for “The” substitute  “Subject to paragraph (1A), the” ;

50.9.b

after paragraph (1) insert—

50.9.b.1A

Paragraphs (1A) to (1M) of rule 28 apply in the case of a voter or proxy who
applies under paragraph (a) as they apply in the case of a voter or proxy who
applies under rule 28(1), but as if—

50.9.b.1A.a

references to delivering a ballot paper to a voter or proxy were to causing a
voter’s or proxy’s vote to be marked on a ballot paper, and

50.9.b.1A.b

in rule 28(1G), the reference to paragraph (1) of rule 28 were to paragraph
(1) of this rule.

.

50.10

In rule 30 (voting by persons with disabilities)—

50.10.a

50.10.b

after paragraph (2) insert—

50.10.b.2A

Paragraphs (1A) to (1M) of rule 28 apply in the case of a voter or proxy who
applies under paragraph (a) as they apply in the case of a voter or proxy who
applies under rule 28(1), but as if—

50.10.b.2A.a

50.10.b.2A.b

in rule 28(1G), the reference to paragraph (1) of rule 28 were to paragraph

.

50.11.7

.

50.12

After rule 32 (tendered ballot papers: general provisions) insert—

########## Refusal to deliver ballot paper

50.12.32A

50.12.32A.1

Where a presiding officer refuses to deliver a ballot paper to a voter who
applied for one other than as a proxy, the officer or a clerk must enter on
the ballot paper refusal list—

50.12.32A.1.a

the voter’s electoral number, and

50.12.32A.1.b

against that number, the reason for the refusal.

50.12.32A.2

Where a presiding officer refuses to deliver a ballot paper to a voter who
applied for one as a proxy, the officer or a clerk must enter on the ballot
paper refusal list—

50.12.32A.2.a

the name and address of the voter, and

50.12.32A.2.b

against those details, the reason for the refusal.

50.12.32A.3

Paragraphs (4) and (5) apply where—

50.12.32A.3.a

a presiding officer refuses to deliver a ballot paper to a voter or proxy
under rule 28(1E), and

50.12.32A.3.b

the voter or proxy makes a further application under rule 28(1).

50.12.32A.4

If a ballot paper is delivered to the voter or proxy following a further
application, the presiding officer or a clerk must note that fact on the
ballot paper refusal list.

50.12.32A.5

If the presiding officer again refuses to deliver a ballot paper to the voter
or proxy, the presiding officer or a clerk must note that fact on the ballot
paper refusal list.

50.12.32A.6

Entries required by this rule to be made on the ballot paper refusal list must
be made as soon as practicable after delivery of a ballot paper to a voter or
proxy is refused (or, in the case mentioned in paragraph (4), as soon as
practicable after the delivery of a ballot paper to a voter or proxy).

50.12.32A.7

For the purposes of paragraph (1)(a), a person’s “electoral number” is the
number—

50.12.32A.7.a

allocated to the person as stated in the copy of the register of electors, or

50.12.32A.7.b

where an entry relating to the person is added to the register in pursuance of
a notice issued under section 13B(3B) or (3D) of the 1983 Act, as stated in
the copy of that notice.

50.12.32A.8

Subject to rule 28(1G) and paragraph (9), a refusal to deliver a ballot paper
to a voter or proxy is final and may not be questioned in any proceeding
whatsoever.

50.12.32A.9

A refusal to deliver a ballot paper to a voter or proxy is subject to review
on a referendum petition.

50.12.32A.10

In this rule—

50.12.32A.10.a

except in paragraph (3)(a), any reference to the refusal to deliver a ballot
paper (however expressed) is to the refusal to do so under rule 26(3) or
28(1E), and

50.12.32A.10.b

any reference to paragraph (1E) or (1G) of rule 28 includes a reference to
that paragraph as applied by rule 29, 30 or 31.

.

(d) insert—

50.13.da

the ballot paper refusal list completed in accordance with rule 32A;

.

50.14

(a) insert—

50.14.aa

the completed ballot paper refusal list; or

.

50.15

In rule 45 (delivery of documents to relevant registration officer), in
paragraph (1) after sub-paragraph (d) insert—

50.15.da

the packet containing the completed ballot paper refusal list;

.

50.16

In rule 46 (orders for production of documents), after paragraph (1) insert—

50.16.1A

An order—

50.16.1A.a

for the opening of the sealed packet containing a completed ballot paper
refusal list, or

50.16.1A.b

for the inspection or production of that list,

may be made by the county court if satisfied by evidence on oath that the
order is required for the purpose of a referendum petition.

.

In Part 8 (appendix of forms)—

50.17.a

in the list of forms, after the entry “Official Proxy Postal Poll Card (to be

52.8.b.1A

A ballot paper must not be delivered to a voter or proxy unless the voter or
proxy produces a specified document to the presiding officer or a clerk.

52.8.b.1B

The presiding officer or clerk must arrange for the voter or proxy to produce
any document in a private area of the polling station if the voter or proxy so
requests, and, in such a case, must ensure that no other persons witness the
production except as permitted by the voter or proxy.

52.8.b.1C

Paragraph (1D) applies in relation to a voter or proxy where—

52.8.b.1C.a

the voter or proxy produces a specified document to a clerk and the clerk
decides that the document raises a reasonable doubt as to whether the voter or
proxy is the voter or proxy that the voter or proxy claims to be, or

52.8.b.1C.b

the voter or proxy produces a document to a clerk that the clerk reasonably
suspects to be a forged document.

52.8.b.1D

had produced the document to the presiding officer in the first place.

52.8.b.1E

proxy where—

52.8.b.1E.a

the voter or proxy produces a specified document to the officer and the
officer decides that the document raises a reasonable doubt as to whether the
voter or proxy is the voter or proxy that the voter or proxy claims to be, or

52.8.b.1E.b

the voter or proxy produces a document to the officer that the officer
reasonably suspects to be a forged document.

52.8.b.1F

52.8.b.1F.a

a discrepancy between the name of the holder of a specified document and the
name of the voter or proxy that the voter or proxy claims to be is resolved to
the presiding officer’s satisfaction at the time of the application by the
voter or proxy producing further proof of identity, and

52.8.b.1F.b

the presiding officer has no other reason (arising from any document produced
by the voter or proxy) to doubt that the voter or proxy is the voter or proxy
that the voter or proxy claims to be.

52.8.b.1G

The refusal to deliver a ballot paper to a voter or proxy under paragraph (1E)
does not prevent the voter or proxy making a further application under
paragraph (1), and paragraphs (1A) to (1F) apply on any further application.

52.8.b.1H

In this rule, a “ forged document ” means a false document made to resemble a
specified document.

52.8.b.1I

In this rule, a “specified document”—

52.8.b.1I.a

except in the case of a voter or proxy who has an anonymous entry in the
register of electors, is one which for the time being falls within the list
specified in rule 37(1H) of Schedule 1 to the 1983 Act (parliamentary election
rules);

52.8.b.1I.b

in the case of a voter or proxy who has an anonymous entry in the register of
electors, means an anonymous elector’s document which—

52.8.b.1I.b.i

was issued by the registration officer for the local authority in whose area
the referendum is held, and

52.8.b.1I.b.ii

contains the number—

52.8.b.1I.b.ii.aa

allocated to the voter or proxy as stated in the copy of the register of
electors, or

52.8.b.1I.b.ii.bb

where an entry relating to the voter or proxy is added to the register in
pursuance of a notice issued under section 13B(3B) or (3D) of the 1983 Act, as
stated in the copy of that notice.

52.8.b.1J

Subject to paragraph (1K), a reference in this rule to a document that is a
specified document is a reference to the document regardless of any expiry
date relating to it.

52.8.b.1K

Paragraph (1J) does not apply to a temporary electoral identity document where
the date of the poll for the referendum is after the date for which the
document is issued.

52.8.b.1L

No person other than the presiding officer or a clerk may inspect a document
produced as proof of a voter’s or proxy’s identity, except as permitted by the
voter or proxy.

52.8.b.1M

References in this rule to producing a document are to producing it for
inspection.

;

52.8.c

in paragraph (2), omit the words from “and only” to the end;

52.8.d

omit paragraph (3)(a).

52.9

In rule 27 (votes marked by the presiding officer)—

52.9.a

in paragraph (1), for “The” substitute  “Subject to paragraph (1A), the” ;

52.9.b

after paragraph (1) insert—

52.9.b.1A

Paragraphs (1A) to (1M) of rule 26 apply in the case of a voter or proxy who
applies under paragraph (a) as they apply in the case of a voter or proxy who
applies under rule 26(1), but as if—

52.9.b.1A.a

references to delivering a ballot paper to a voter or proxy were to causing a
voter’s or proxy’s vote to be marked on a ballot paper, and

52.9.b.1A.b

in rule 26(1G), the reference to paragraph (1) of rule 26 were to paragraph
(1) of this rule.

.

52.10

In rule 28 (voting by persons with disabilities)—

52.10.a

in paragraph (2), for “If” substitute  “Subject to paragraph (2A), if” ;

52.10.b

after paragraph (2) insert—

52.10.b.2A

Paragraphs (1A) to (1M) of rule 26 apply in the case of a voter or proxy who
applies under paragraph (a) as they apply in the case of a voter or proxy who
applies under rule 26(1), but as if—

52.10.b.2A.a

references to delivering a ballot paper to a voter or proxy were to granting a
voter’s or proxy’s application, and

52.10.b.2A.b

in rule 26(1G), the reference to paragraph (1) of rule 26 were to paragraph
(1) of this rule.

.

52.11

In rule 29 (tendered ballot papers: circumstances where available), after

52.11.7

Paragraphs (1A) to (1M) of rule 26 apply in the case of a person who seeks to

rule 26(1G), the reference to making a further application under paragraph (1)
of rule 26 were to seeking a further time to mark a tendered ballot paper
under the paragraph of this rule under which a previous such attempt was made.

.

52.12

After rule 30 (tendered ballot papers: general provisions) insert—

########## Refusal to deliver ballot paper

52.12.30A

52.12.30A.1

Where a presiding officer refuses to deliver a ballot paper to a voter who
applied for one other than as a proxy, the officer or a clerk must enter on
the ballot paper refusal list—

52.12.30A.1.a

the voter’s electoral number, and

52.12.30A.1.b

against that number, the reason for the refusal.

52.12.30A.2

Where a presiding officer refuses to deliver a ballot paper to a voter who
applied for one as a proxy, the officer or a clerk must enter on the ballot
paper refusal list—

52.12.30A.2.a

the name and address of the voter, and

52.12.30A.2.b

against those details, the reason for the refusal.

52.12.30A.3

Paragraphs (4) and (5) apply where—

52.12.30A.3.a

a presiding officer refuses to deliver a ballot paper to a voter or proxy
under rule 26(1E), and

52.12.30A.3.b

the voter or proxy makes a further application under rule 26(1).

52.12.30A.4

If a ballot paper is delivered to the voter or proxy following a further
application, the presiding officer or a clerk must note that fact on the
ballot paper refusal list.

52.12.30A.5

If the presiding officer again refuses to deliver a ballot paper to the voter
or proxy, the presiding officer or a clerk must note that fact on the ballot
paper refusal list.

52.12.30A.6

Entries required by this rule to be made on the ballot paper refusal list must
be made as soon as practicable after delivery of a ballot paper to a voter or
proxy is refused (or, in the case mentioned in paragraph (4), as soon as
practicable after the delivery of a ballot paper to a voter or proxy).

52.12.30A.7

For the purposes of paragraph (1)(a), a person’s “electoral number” is the
number—

52.12.30A.7.a

allocated to the person as stated in the copy of the register of electors, or

52.12.30A.7.b

where an entry relating to the person is added to the register in pursuance of
a notice issued under section 13B(3B) or (3D) of the 1983 Act, as stated in
the copy of that notice.

52.12.30A.8

Subject to rule 26(1G) and paragraph (9), a refusal to deliver a ballot paper
to a voter or proxy is final and may not be questioned in any proceeding
whatsoever.

52.12.30A.9

A refusal to deliver a ballot paper to a voter or proxy is subject to review
on a referendum petition.

52.12.30A.10

In this rule—

52.12.30A.10.a

except in paragraph (3)(a), any reference to the refusal to deliver a ballot
paper (however expressed) is to the refusal to do so under rule 24(3) or
26(1E), and

52.12.30A.10.b

any reference to paragraph (1E) or (1G) of rule 26 includes a reference to
that paragraph as applied by rule 27, 28 or 29.

.

.

52.14.ba

the completed ballot paper refusal list;

.

52.15

In rule 43 (delivery of documents to relevant registration officer), in

the packet containing the completed ballot paper refusal list;

.

52.16.1A

52.16.1A.a

for the opening of the sealed packet containing a completed ballot paper
refusal list, or

52.16.1A.b

for the inspection or production of that list,

may be made by the county court if satisfied by evidence on oath that the
order is required for the purpose of a referendum petition.

.

54.7.b.2A

54.7.c.3.a

54.7.c.3.c

32A for the procedure where a ballot paper is refused under this paragraph).

54.7.c.3A.b

54.8.b.1A

A ballot paper must not be delivered to a voter or proxy unless the voter or
proxy produces a specified document to the presiding officer or a clerk.

54.8.b.1B

The presiding officer or clerk must arrange for the voter or proxy to produce
any document in a private area of the polling station if the voter or proxy so

production except as permitted by the voter or proxy.

54.8.b.1C

54.8.b.1C.a

voter or proxy is the voter or proxy that the voter or proxy claims to be, or

the voter or proxy produces a document to the officer that the officer
reasonably suspects to be a forged document.

54.8.b.1F

54.8.b.1F.a

a discrepancy between the name of the holder of a specified document and the

54.8.b.1F.b

the presiding officer has no other reason (arising from any document produced
by the voter or proxy) to doubt that the voter or proxy is the voter or proxy
that the voter or proxy claims to be.

54.8.b.1G

54.8.b.1I.b.i

########## Refusal to deliver ballot paper

54.12.32A

54.12.32A.1

Where a presiding officer refuses to deliver a ballot paper to a voter who
applied for one other than as a proxy, the officer or a clerk must enter on
the ballot paper refusal list—

54.12.32A.1.a

the voter’s electoral number, and

54.12.32A.1.b

against that number, the reason for the refusal.

54.12.32A.2

Where a presiding officer refuses to deliver a ballot paper to a voter who
applied for one as a proxy, the officer or a clerk must enter on the ballot
paper refusal list—

54.12.32A.2.a

the name and address of the voter, and

54.12.32A.2.b

against those details, the reason for the refusal.

54.12.32A.3

Paragraphs (4) and (5) apply where—

54.12.32A.3.a

a presiding officer refuses to deliver a ballot paper to a voter or proxy
under rule 28(1E), and

54.12.32A.3.b

the voter or proxy makes a further application under rule 28(1).

54.12.32A.4

If a ballot paper is delivered to the voter or proxy following a further
application, the presiding officer or a clerk must note that fact on the
ballot paper refusal list.

54.12.32A.5

If the presiding officer again refuses to deliver a ballot paper to the voter
or proxy, the presiding officer or a clerk must note that fact on the ballot
paper refusal list.

54.12.32A.6

Entries required by this rule to be made on the ballot paper refusal list must
be made as soon as practicable after delivery of a ballot paper to a voter or
proxy is refused (or, in the case mentioned in paragraph (4), as soon as
practicable after the delivery of a ballot paper to a voter or proxy).

54.12.32A.7

number—

54.12.32A.7.a

allocated to the person as stated in the copy of the register of electors, or

54.12.32A.7.b

where an entry relating to the person is added to the register in pursuance of
a notice issued under section 13B(3B) or (3D) of the 1983 Act, as stated in
the copy of that notice.

54.12.32A.8

Subject to rule 28(1G) and paragraph (9), a refusal to deliver a ballot paper
to a voter or proxy is final and may not be questioned in any proceeding
whatsoever.

54.12.32A.9

A refusal to deliver a ballot paper to a voter or proxy is subject to review
on a referendum petition.

54.12.32A.10

In this rule—

54.12.32A.10.a

except in paragraph (3)(a), any reference to the refusal to deliver a ballot
paper (however expressed) is to the refusal to do so under rule 26(3) or
28(1E), and

54.12.32A.10.b

any reference to paragraph (1E) or (1G) of rule 28 includes a reference to
that paragraph as applied by rule 29, 30 or 31.

#### Amendment of Schedule 2 (absent voting in PCC elections)

############ Additional requirements: applications for the appointment of a proxy on grounds relation to voter identification

59.2.b.14A

59.2.b.14A.1

This paragraph applies where—

59.2.b.14A.1.a

an application under paragraph 5(4) for the appointment of a proxy for the
purposes of voting by proxy at a particular PCC election is made by a person
(“ A ”);

59.2.b.14A.1.b

A has previously appointed a person (“ B ”) as A’s proxy for those purposes;

59.2.b.14A.1.c

at the time of making the application, B’s appointment remains in force; and

59.2.b.14A.1.d

A’s application is made on grounds relating to voter identification which
relate to B.

59.2.b.14A.2

A’s application must—

59.2.b.14A.2.a

state that this paragraph applies, and

59.2.b.14A.2.b

state, to the best of A’s knowledge and belief, which of the conditions set
out in paragraph 16A apply in respect of B.
