in paragraph (a), the reference to an application under paragraph 5(4)
includes such an application which is included in an application under
paragraph 3(2);

59.2.b.14A.3.b

in paragraph (d), “ grounds relating to voter identification ” has the meaning
given in paragraph 16A.

.

59.2.c

after paragraph 15A (additional requirements referred to in paragraph 14(5A))
insert—

############ Additional requirements for an application under paragraph 3(2) for a proxy vote: grounds related to voter identification

59.2.c.15B

59.2.c.15B.1

Subject to sub-paragraph (2), this paragraph applies to an application under
paragraph 3(2) to which paragraph 16(2C) applies.

59.2.c.15B.2

This paragraph does not apply where—

59.2.c.15B.2.a

the application under paragraph 3(2) includes an application under paragraph
5(4), and

59.2.c.15B.2.b

paragraph 14A(2) applies to that application under paragraph 5(4).

59.2.c.15B.3

Where this paragraph applies, the application under paragraph 3(2) must (in
addition to any other information required by this Part)—

59.2.c.15B.3.a

state that it is made on grounds relating to voter identification, and

59.2.c.15B.3.b

states which of the conditions set out in paragraph 16A apply to the
applicant.

59.2.c.15B.4

In this paragraph, “ grounds relating to voter identification ” has the
meaning given in paragraph 16A.

;

59.2.d

in paragraph 16 (closing date for applications)—

59.2.d.i

in sub-paragraph (1), after “sub-paragraph (2)” insert  “and (2C)” ;

59.2.d.ii

before sub-paragraph (3) insert—

59.2.d.ii.2C

Where an application is made under paragraph 3(2) or 5(4) on grounds relating
to voter identification, the application is to be refused if it is received
after 5pm on the day of the poll at the PCC election for which it is made.

59.2.d.ii.2D

In sub-paragraph (2C), “ grounds relating to voter identification ” has the
meaning given in paragraph 16A.

;

59.2.e

after paragraph 16 insert—

############ Grounds relating to voter identification

59.2.e.16A

59.2.e.16A.1

For the purposes of this Part, an application is made on grounds relating to
voter identification if it is made because the following apply to B—

59.2.e.16A.1.a

condition 1, 2, 3 or 4, and

59.2.e.16A.1.b

except where B has an anonymous entry on the register of electors, condition
5.

59.2.e.16A.2

In this paragraph, “ B ” means—

59.2.e.16A.2.a

the applicant, where—

59.2.e.16A.2.a.i

the application is made under paragraph 3(2), and

59.2.e.16A.2.a.ii

paragraph 14A(2) does not apply to the application made under paragraph 5(4)
which is included in that application under paragraph 3(2);

59.2.e.16A.2.b

otherwise, the person already appointed as the applicant’s proxy at the time
the application is made.

59.2.e.16A.3

Condition 1 is that—

59.2.e.16A.3.a

immediately before the deadline, B has a specified document which B intends to
use to vote in person at a PCC election, and

59.2.e.16A.3.b

after that deadline, that document is—

59.2.e.16A.3.b.i

lost, stolen, destroyed or damaged so as to be no longer usable as a specified
document for the purposes of that election, or

59.2.e.16A.3.b.ii

sent by B to another person to prove B’s identity and B considers that it is
unlikely to be returned to B on or before the day of poll at that election.

59.2.e.16A.4

Condition 2 is that—

59.2.e.16A.4.a

at a time during the period of 3 months ending with the deadline, B has
applied for a specified document,

59.2.e.16A.4.b

immediately before the deadline, B has not received that document, and

59.2.e.16A.4.c

the application for the specified document has not been refused or withdrawn.

59.2.e.16A.5

Condition 3 is that—

59.2.e.16A.5.a

B has an anonymous entry on the register of electors, and

59.2.e.16A.5.b

either—

59.2.e.16A.5.b.i

B has not been issued with an anonymous elector’s document, or

59.2.e.16A.5.b.ii

B has been issued with an anonymous elector’s document, and after the deadline
B is allocated an electoral number which is different from the one shown on
that document other than as a result of an application under section 9B of the
1983 Act (anonymous registration).

59.2.e.16A.6

Condition 4 is that—

59.2.e.16A.6.a

B has a temporary electoral identity document which is valid for use on the
day of poll at a PCC election, and

59.2.e.16A.6.b

before B is able to vote in person at such an election using that document,
proceedings at B’s polling station are adjourned in accordance with rule 46 of
Part 3 of Schedule 3 (adjournment of poll in case of riot).

59.2.e.16A.7

Condition 5 is that B does not have access to another specified document.

59.2.e.16A.8

In this paragraph—

59.2.e.16A.8.a

“anonymous elector’s document” and “temporary electoral identity document”
have the meanings given in regulation  3(1)  of the Voter Identification
Regulations 2022;

59.2.e.16A.8.b

the “ deadline ” means 5 pm on the sixth day before the date of the poll at
the PCC election for which an application is made, and paragraph 16(5) applies
for the purposes of computing the sixth day as it applies for the purposes of
computing a period of days for the purposes of paragraph 16;

59.2.e.16A.8.c

“ specified document ” has the meaning given in rule 39(2I) of Part 3 of
Schedule 3.

.

in the case of an elector (other than an elector with an anonymous entry) or a

60.5

In rule 37 (questions to be put to voters)—

60.5.a

in the table following paragraph (1), in the column headed “Question”, in
entry 1 (electors), entry 2 (proxies), entry 3 (proxies for an elector with an
anonymous entry), entry 5 (postal voters) and entry 6 (proxy postal voters),
before question (a) insert—

60.5.a.za

What is your name?

60.5.a.zb

What is your address?

;

60.5.b

after paragraph (2) insert—

60.5.b.2A

Where a clerk—

60.5.b.2A.a

gives a person the required information (see paragraph (5)),

60.5.b.2A.b

puts a question specified in paragraph (1) to the person, and

60.5.b.2A.c

decides that the person has failed to answer the question satisfactorily,

the clerk must refer the matter to the presiding officer, who must put the
question to the person again.

;

60.5.c

for paragraph (3) substitute—

60.5.c.3

Where the presiding officer—

60.5.c.3.a

gives a person the required information,

60.5.c.3.b

puts a question specified in paragraph (1) to the person (whether or not
following a referral under paragraph (2A)), and

60.5.c.3.c

decides that the person has failed to answer the question satisfactorily,

the officer must refuse to deliver a ballot paper to the person (and see rule
43A (procedure where ballot paper is refused under this paragraph)).

60.5.c.3A

For the purposes of this rule, a person answers the question “What is your
name?” or “What is your address?” satisfactorily if—

60.5.c.3A.a

where one of those questions is put, the answer matches a name or address (as
the case may be) in the register of local government electors;

60.5.c.3A.b

where both those questions are put, the answers match a name and address in
that register that relate to the same person.

60.5.c.3B

In the case of an elector in respect of whom a notice has been issued under
section 13B(3B) or (3D) of the 1983 Act, the references to the register in
paragraph (3C) are to be read as references to the notice issued under section
13B(3B) or (3D).

;

60.5.d

in paragraph (4), after “vote” insert  “(and for the purposes of this
paragraph, an inquiry relating to the production of identification by a voter
is not to be regarded as an inquiry as to the right of the person to vote)” ;

60.5.e

after paragraph (4) insert—

60.5.e.5

For the purposes of this rule, a person to whom any question is to be put is
given “the required information” if the person is first informed that—

60.5.e.5.a

a ballot paper will be refused if the person fails to answer each question
satisfactorily, and

60.5.e.5.b

giving false information may be an offence.

.

60.6

In rule 39 (voting procedure)—

60.6.a

in paragraph (1), for “A” substitute  “Subject to rule 37(3) and to paragraphs
(2A) to (2M), a” ;

60.6.b

omit paragraph (2)(a);

60.6.c

after paragraph (2) insert—

60.6.c.2A

A ballot paper must not be delivered to a voter unless the voter produces a
specified document to the presiding officer or a clerk.

60.6.c.2B

The presiding officer or clerk must arrange for the voter to produce any
document in a private area of the polling station if the voter so requests,
and, in such a case, must ensure that no other persons witness the production
except as permitted by the voter.

60.6.c.2C

Paragraph (2D) applies in relation to a voter where—

60.6.c.2C.a

the voter produces a specified document to a clerk and the clerk decides that
the document raises a reasonable doubt as to whether the voter is the elector
or proxy that the voter claims to be, or

60.6.c.2C.b

the voter produces a document to a clerk that the clerk reasonably suspects to
be a forged document.

60.6.c.2D

Where this paragraph applies, the clerk must refer the matter and produce the
document to the presiding officer, who must proceed as if the voter had
produced the document to the presiding officer in the first place.

60.6.c.2E

The presiding officer must refuse to deliver a ballot paper to a voter where—

60.6.c.2E.a

the voter produces a specified document to the officer and the officer decides
that the document raises a reasonable doubt as to whether the voter is the
elector or proxy that the voter claims to be, or

60.6.c.2E.b

the voter produces a document to the officer that the officer reasonably
suspects to be a forged document.

60.6.c.2F

Paragraph (2E)(a) does not apply where—

60.6.c.2F.a

a discrepancy between the name of the holder of a specified document and the
name of the elector or proxy that the voter claims to be is resolved to the
presiding officer’s satisfaction at the time of the application by the voter
producing further proof of identity, and

60.6.c.2F.b

the presiding officer has no other reason (arising from any document produced
by the voter) to doubt that the voter is the elector or proxy that the voter
claims to be.

60.6.c.2G

The refusal to deliver a ballot paper to a voter under paragraph (2E) does not
prevent the voter making a further application under paragraph (1), and
paragraphs (2A) to (2F) apply on any further application.

60.6.c.2H

In this rule, a “ forged document ” means a false document made to resemble a
specified document.

60.6.c.2I

In this rule, a “specified document”—

60.6.c.2I.a

except in the case of a voter who has an anonymous entry in the register of
electors, means a document which for the time being falls within the list
specified in rule 37(1H) of Schedule 1 to the 1983 Act (parliamentary election
rules);

60.6.c.2I.b

in the case of a voter who has an anonymous entry in the register of electors,
means an anonymous elector’s document which—

60.6.c.2I.b.i

was issued by the relevant registration officer for the voting area in which
the polling station to which the voter is allotted is situated,

60.6.c.2I.b.ii

contains the number—

60.6.c.2I.b.ii.aa

allocated to the voter as stated in the copy of the register of electors, or

60.6.c.2I.b.ii.bb

where an entry relating to the voter is added to the register in pursuance of
a notice issued under section 13B(3B) or (3D) of the 1983 Act, as stated in
the copy of that notice.

60.6.c.2J

Subject to paragraph (2K), a reference in this rule to a document that is a
specified document is a reference to the document regardless of any expiry
date relating to it.

60.6.c.2K

Paragraph (2J) does not apply to a temporary electoral identity document where
the date of the poll for the election is after the date for which the document
is issued.

60.6.c.2L

No person other than the presiding officer or a clerk may inspect a document
produced as proof of a voter’s identity, except as permitted by the voter.

60.6.c.2M

References in this rule to producing a document are to producing it for
inspection.

;

60.6.d

in paragraph (3), omit the words from “and only” until the end;

60.6.e

omit paragraph (4)(a).

60.7.a

Paragraphs (2A) to (2M) of rule 39 apply in the case of a voter who applies

60.7.b.2A.a

60.10

After rule 43 (tendered ballot papers: general provisions) insert—

########## Refusal to deliver ballot paper

60.10.43A

60.10.43A.1

Where a presiding officer refuses to deliver a ballot paper to a voter who
applied for one as an elector, the officer or a clerk must enter on the ballot
paper refusal list—

60.10.43A.1.a

the voter’s electoral number, and

60.10.43A.1.b

against that number, the reason for the refusal.

60.10.43A.2

Where a presiding officer refuses to deliver a ballot paper to a voter who
applied for one as a proxy, the officer or a clerk must enter on the ballot
paper refusal list—

60.10.43A.2.a

the name and address of the voter, and

60.10.43A.2.b

against those details, the reason for the refusal.

60.10.43A.3

Paragraphs (4) and (5) apply where—

60.10.43A.3.a

a presiding officer refuses to deliver a ballot paper to a voter under rule
39(2E), and

60.10.43A.3.b

the voter makes a further application as permitted by rule 39(2G).

60.10.43A.4

If a ballot paper is delivered to the voter following that application, the
presiding officer or a clerk must note that fact on the ballot paper refusal
list.

60.10.43A.5

If the presiding officer again refuses to deliver a ballot paper to the voter,
the presiding officer or a clerk must note that fact on the ballot paper
refusal list.

60.10.43A.6

Entries required by this rule to be made on the ballot paper refusal list must
be made as soon as practicable after delivery of a ballot paper to a voter is
refused (or, in the case mentioned in paragraph (4), as soon as practicable
after the delivery of a ballot paper to a voter).

60.10.43A.7

For the purposes of paragraph (1)(a), a person’s “electoral number” is the
number—

60.10.43A.7.a

allocated to the person as stated in the copy of the register of electors, or

60.10.43A.7.b

where an entry relating to the person is added to the register in pursuance of
a notice issued under section 13B(3B) or (3D) of the 1983 Act, as stated in
the copy of that notice.

60.10.43A.8

Subject to rule 39(2G) and paragraph (9), a refusal to deliver a ballot paper
to a voter is final and may not be questioned in any proceeding whatsoever.

60.10.43A.9

A refusal to deliver a ballot paper to a voter is subject to review on an
election petition.

60.10.43A.10

In this rule—

60.10.43A.10.a

except in paragraph (3)(a), any reference to the refusal to deliver a ballot
paper (however expressed) is to the refusal to do so under rule 37(3) or
39(2E), and

60.10.43A.10.b

any reference to paragraph (2E) or (2G) of rule 39 includes a reference to
that paragraph as applied by rule 40, 41 or 42.

.

(d) insert—

60.11.da

the ballot paper refusal list completed in accordance with rule 43A,

.

60.12.aa

the completed ballot paper refusal list,

.

60.13.ca

In rule 67 (orders for production of documents), after paragraph (1) insert—

An order—

for the opening of the sealed packet containing a completed ballot paper

60.14.1A.b

for the inspection or production of that list,

may be made by the county court if satisfied by evidence on oath that the

#### Amendment of Schedule 3 (neighbourhood planning referendum rules)

64

64.1

Schedule 3 (neighbourhood planning referendum rules) is amended as follows.

64.2

In the list of contents, at the appropriate place insert  “31A Refusal to
deliver ballot paper” .

64.3

In rule 2 (interpretation), for paragraph (1) substitute—

64.3.1

In these Rules—

      “anonymous elector’s document” and “temporary electoral identity
document” have the meanings given in regulation  3(1)  of the Voter
Identification Regulations 2022;           “ voter ” means a person entitled
to vote on their own behalf.

.

64.4

In rule 15 (provision of polling stations), after paragraph (4) insert—

64.4.5

The counting officer must ensure that each polling station contains an area in
which voters and proxies can produce proof of identity in private.

In rule 16 (appointment of presiding officers and polling clerks), in
paragraph (3) for the words from “except” to the end substitute—

except—

64.5.a

64.5.b

refuse to deliver a ballot paper under rule 25(3) or rule 27(1E) (including

64.5.c

resolve doubts over identity as mentioned in rule 27(1F) (including that

.

64.6

In rule 18 (equipment of polling stations)—

64.6.a

in paragraph (5)—

64.6.a.i

64.6.a.ii

after sub-paragraph (a) insert—

64.6.a.ii.aa

a ballot paper refusal list, set out in Form 10A in the Appendix or a form to
like effect, on which entries are to be made as mentioned in rule 31A (refusal
to deliver ballot paper); and

;

64.6.b

after paragraph (6) insert—

64.6.b.6A

A large notice must be displayed inside each polling station containing—

64.6.b.6A.a

details of the documents the voter or proxy needs to produce when applying for
a ballot paper, namely—

64.6.b.6A.a.i

in the case of a voter (other than a voter with an anonymous entry) or a
proxy, any of the forms of identification for the time being referred to in
rule 37(1H) of Schedule 1 to the 1983 Act (parliamentary elections rules);

64.6.b.6A.a.ii

in the case of a voter with an anonymous entry, the voter’s official poll card
and an anonymous elector’s document showing the same electoral number as the
electoral number shown on the official poll card; and

64.6.b.6A.b

a statement that further proof of identity may be required to resolve any
discrepancy between the name of the holder of a form of identification and the
name of the voter or proxy that the voter or proxy claims to be.

.

64.7

In rule 25 (questions to be put to voters and proxies)—

64.7.a

in the table following paragraph (1), in the column headed “Questions”, in
entry 1 (voters), entry 2 (proxies), entry 3 (proxies for a voter with an
anonymous entry), entry 5 (postal voters) and entry 6 (proxy postal voters),
before question (a) insert—

64.7.a.za

What is your name?

64.7.a.zb

What is your address?

;

64.7.b

after paragraph (2) insert—

64.7.b.2A

Where a clerk—

64.7.b.2A.a

gives a person the required information (see paragraph (5)),

64.7.b.2A.b

puts a question specified in paragraph (1) to the person, and

64.7.b.2A.c

decides that the person has failed to answer the question satisfactorily,

the clerk must refer the matter to the presiding officer, who must put the
question to the person again.

;

64.7.c

for paragraph (3) substitute—

64.7.c.3

Where the presiding officer—

64.7.c.3.a

gives the person the required information,

64.7.c.3.b

puts a question specified in paragraph (1) to the person (whether or not
following a referral under paragraph (2A)), and

64.7.c.3.c

decides that the person has failed to answer the question satisfactorily,

the officer must refuse to deliver a ballot paper to the person (and see rule
31A for the procedure where a ballot paper is refused under this paragraph).

64.7.c.3A

For the purposes of this rule, a person answers the question “What is your
name?” or “What is your address?” satisfactorily if—

64.7.c.3A.a

where one of those questions is put, the answer matches a name or address (as
the case may be) in the register of electors;

64.7.c.3A.b

where both those questions are put, the answers match a name and address in
that register that relate to the same person.

64.7.c.3B

In the case of a voter or proxy in respect of whom a notice has been issued
under section 13B(3B) or (3D) of the 1983 Act, the references to the register
in paragraph (3A) are to be read as references to the notice issued under
section 13B(3B) or (3D).

;

64.7.d

in paragraph (4), after “vote” insert  “(and for the purposes of this
paragraph, an inquiry relating to the production of identification by a voter
or proxy is not to be regarded as an inquiry as to the right of the person to
vote)” ;

64.7.e

after paragraph (4) insert—

64.7.e.5

For the purposes of this rule, a person to whom any question is to be put is
given “the required information” if the person is first informed that—

64.7.e.5.a

a ballot paper will be refused if the person fails to answer each question
satisfactorily, and

64.7.e.5.b

giving false information may be an offence.

.

64.8

In rule 27 (voting procedure)—

64.8.a

in paragraph (1)—

64.8.a.i

for “A” substitute  “Subject to rule 25(3) and to paragraphs (1A) to (1M), a”
;

64.8.a.ii

omit sub-paragraph (a);

64.8.b

after paragraph (1) insert—

64.8.b.1A

A ballot paper must not be delivered to a voter or proxy unless the voter or
proxy produces a specified document to the presiding officer or a clerk.

64.8.b.1B

The presiding officer or clerk must arrange for the voter or proxy to produce
any document in a private area of the polling station if the voter or proxy so
requests, and, in such a case, must ensure that no other persons witness the
production except as permitted by the voter or proxy.

64.8.b.1C

Paragraph (1D) applies in relation to a voter or proxy where—

64.8.b.1C.a

the voter or proxy produces a specified document to a clerk and the clerk
decides that the document raises a reasonable doubt as to whether the voter or
proxy is the voter or proxy that the voter or proxy claims to be, or

64.8.b.1C.b

the voter or proxy produces a document to a clerk that the clerk reasonably
suspects to be a forged document.

64.8.b.1D

Where this paragraph applies, the clerk must refer the matter and produce the
document to the presiding officer, who must proceed as if the voter or proxy
had produced the document to the presiding officer in the first place.

64.8.b.1E

The presiding officer must refuse to deliver a ballot paper to a voter or
proxy where—

64.8.b.1E.a

the voter or proxy produces a specified document to the officer and the
officer decides that the document raises a reasonable doubt as to whether the
voter or proxy is the voter or proxy that the voter or proxy claims to be, or

64.8.b.1E.b

the voter or proxy produces a document to the officer that the officer
reasonably suspects to be a forged document.

64.8.b.1F

Paragraph (1E)(a) does not apply where—

64.8.b.1F.a

a discrepancy between the name of the holder of a specified document and the
name of the voter or proxy that the voter or proxy claims to be is resolved to
the presiding officer’s satisfaction at the time of the application by the
voter or proxy producing further proof of identity, and

64.8.b.1F.b

the presiding officer has no other reason (arising from any document produced
by the voter or proxy) to doubt that the voter or proxy is the voter or proxy
that the voter or proxy claims to be.

64.8.b.1G

The refusal to deliver a ballot paper to a voter or proxy under paragraph (1E)
does not prevent the voter or proxy making a further application under
paragraph (1), and paragraphs (1A) to (1F) apply on any further application.

64.8.b.1H

In this rule, a “ forged document ” means a false document made to resemble a
specified document.

64.8.b.1I

In this rule, a “specified document”—

64.8.b.1I.a

except in the case of a voter or proxy who has an anonymous entry in the
register of electors, is one which for the time being falls within the list
specified in rule 37(1H) of Schedule 1 to the 1983 Act (parliamentary election
rules);

64.8.b.1I.b

in the case of a voter or proxy who has an anonymous entry in the register of
electors, means an anonymous elector’s document which—

64.8.b.1I.b.i

was issued by the registration officer for the local authority in whose area
the referendum is held,

64.8.b.1I.b.ii

contains the number—

64.8.b.1I.b.ii.aa

allocated to the voter or proxy as stated in the copy of the register of
electors, or

64.8.b.1I.b.ii.bb

where an entry relating to the voter or proxy is added to the register in
pursuance of a notice issued under section 13B(3B) or (3D) of the 1983 Act, as
stated in the copy of that notice.

64.8.b.1J

Subject to paragraph (1K), a reference in this rule to a document that is a
specified document is a reference to the document regardless of any expiry
date relating to it.

64.8.b.1K

Paragraph (1J) does not apply to a temporary electoral identity document where
the date of the poll for the referendum is after the date for which the
document is issued.

64.8.b.1L

No person other than the presiding officer or a clerk may inspect a document
produced as proof of a voter’s identity, except as permitted by the voter.

64.8.b.1M

References in this rule to producing a document are to producing it for
inspection.

;

64.8.c

in paragraph (2), omit the words from “and only” to the end;

64.8.d

omit paragraph (3)(a).

64.9

In rule 28 (votes marked by the presiding officer)—

64.9.a

in paragraph (1), for “The” substitute  “Subject to paragraph (1A), the” ;

64.9.b

after paragraph (1) insert—

64.9.b.1A

Paragraphs (1A) to (1M) of rule 27 apply in the case of a voter or proxy who
applies under paragraph (a) as they apply in the case of a voter or proxy who
applies under rule 27(1), but as if—

64.9.b.1A.a

references to delivering a ballot paper to a voter or proxy were to causing a
voter’s or proxy’s vote to be marked on a ballot paper, and

64.9.b.1A.b

in rule 27(1G), the reference to paragraph (1) of rule 27 were to paragraph
(1) of this rule.

.

64.10

In rule 29 (voting by persons with disabilities)—

64.10.a

in paragraph (2), for “If” substitute  “Subject to paragraph (2A), if” ;

64.10.b

after paragraph (2) insert—

64.10.b.2A

Paragraphs (1A) to (1M) of rule 27 apply in the case of a voter or proxy who
applies under paragraph (a) as they apply in the case of a voter or proxy who
applies under rule 27(1), but as if—

64.10.b.2A.a

references to delivering a ballot paper to a voter or proxy were to granting a
voter’s or proxy’s application, and

64.10.b.2A.b

in rule 27(1G), the reference to paragraph (1) of rule 27 were to paragraph
(1) of this rule.

.

64.11

In rule 30 (tendered ballot papers: circumstances where available), after

64.11.7

Paragraphs (1A) to (1M) of rule 27 apply in the case of a person who seeks to
mark a tendered ballot paper under this rule as they apply in the case of a

rule 27(1G), the reference to making a further application under paragraph (1)
of rule 27 were to seeking a further time to mark a tendered ballot paper
under the paragraph of this rule under which a previous such attempt was made.

.

64.12

After rule 31 (tendered ballot papers: general provisions) insert—

########## Refusal to deliver ballot paper

64.12.31A

64.12.31A.1

Where a presiding officer refuses to deliver a ballot paper to a voter who
applied for one other than as a proxy, the officer or a clerk must enter on
the ballot paper refusal list—

64.12.31A.1.a

the voter’s electoral number, and

64.12.31A.1.b

against that number, the reason for the refusal.

64.12.31A.2

Where a presiding officer refuses to deliver a ballot paper to a voter who
applied for one as a proxy, the officer or a clerk must enter on the ballot
paper refusal list—

64.12.31A.2.a

the name and address of the voter, and

64.12.31A.2.b

against those details, the reason for the refusal.

64.12.31A.3

Paragraphs (4) and (5) apply where—

64.12.31A.3.a

a presiding officer refuses to deliver a ballot paper to a voter or proxy
under rule 27(1E), and

64.12.31A.3.b

the voter or proxy makes a further application under rule 27(1).

64.12.31A.4

If a ballot paper is delivered to the voter or proxy following a further
application, the presiding officer or a clerk must note that fact on the
ballot paper refusal list.

64.12.31A.5

If the presiding officer again refuses to deliver a ballot paper to the voter
or proxy, the presiding officer or a clerk must note that fact on the ballot
paper refusal list.

64.12.31A.6

Entries required by this rule to be made on the ballot paper refusal list must
be made as soon as practicable after delivery of a ballot paper to a voter or
proxy is refused (or, in the case mentioned in paragraph (4), as soon as
practicable after the delivery of a ballot paper to a voter or proxy).

64.12.31A.7

For the purposes of paragraph (1)(a), a person’s “electoral number” is the
number—

64.12.31A.7.a

allocated to the person as stated in the copy of the register of electors, or

64.12.31A.7.b

where an entry relating to the person is added to the register in pursuance of
a notice issued under section 13B(3B) or (3D) of the 1983 Act, as stated in
the copy of that notice.

64.12.31A.8

Subject to rule 27(1G) and paragraph (9), a refusal to deliver a ballot paper
to a voter or proxy is final and may not be questioned in any proceeding
whatsoever.

64.12.31A.9

A refusal to deliver a ballot paper to a voter or proxy is subject to review
in proceedings brought as mentioned in section 61N(3) of the 1990 Act .

64.12.31A.10

In this rule—

64.12.31A.10.a

except in paragraph (3)(a), any reference to the refusal to deliver a ballot
paper (however expressed) is to the refusal to do so under rule 25(3) or
27(1E), and

64.12.31A.10.b

any reference to paragraph (1E) or (1G) of rule 27 includes a reference to
that paragraph as applied by rule 28, 29 or 30.

.

64.13

In rule 35 (procedure on close of poll), in paragraph (1) after sub-paragraph
(d) insert—

64.13.da

the ballot paper refusal list completed in accordance with rule 31A;

.

64.14

In rule 44 (sealing up of ballot papers), in paragraph (2) after sub-paragraph
(b) insert—

64.14.ba

the completed ballot paper refusal list;

.

64.15

In rule 45 (delivery of documents to relevant registration officer), after
paragraph (d) insert—

64.15.da

the packet containing the completed ballot paper refusal list;

.

64.16

In rule 46 (orders for production of documents), after paragraph (1) insert—

64.16.1A

An order—

64.16.1A.a

for the opening of the sealed packet containing a completed ballot paper
refusal list, or

64.16.1A.b

for the inspection or production of that list,

may be made by the High Court or the county court if satisfied by evidence on
oath that the order is required for the purpose of proceedings brought as
mentioned in section 61N(3) of the 1990 Act.

.

In Part 8 (appendix of forms)—

in paragraph (1)—

66.8.a.i

for “A” substitute  “Subject to rule 25(3) and to paragraphs (1A) to (1M), a”
;

66.8.a.ii

omit sub-paragraph (a);

66.8.b

after paragraph (1) insert—

66.8.b.1A

A ballot paper must not be delivered to a voter or proxy unless the voter or
proxy produces a specified document to the presiding officer or a clerk.

66.8.b.1B

The presiding officer or clerk must arrange for the voter or proxy to produce
any document in a private area of the polling station if the voter or proxy so
requests, and, in such a case, must ensure that no other persons witness the
production except as permitted by the voter or proxy.

66.8.b.1C

Paragraph (1D) applies in relation to a voter or proxy where—

66.8.b.1C.a

the voter or proxy produces a specified document to a clerk and the clerk
decides that the document raises a reasonable doubt as to whether the voter or
proxy is the voter or proxy that the voter or proxy claims to be, or

66.8.b.1C.b

the voter or proxy produces a document to a clerk that the clerk reasonably
suspects to be a forged document.

66.8.b.1D

Where this paragraph applies, the clerk must refer the matter and produce the
document to the presiding officer, who must proceed as if the voter or proxy
had produced the document to the presiding officer in the first place.

66.8.b.1E

The presiding officer must refuse to deliver a ballot paper to a voter or
proxy where—

66.8.b.1E.a

the voter or proxy produces a specified document to the officer and the
officer decides that the document raises a reasonable doubt as to whether the
voter or proxy is the voter or proxy that the voter or proxy claims to be, or

66.8.b.1E.b

the voter or proxy produces a document to the officer that the officer
reasonably suspects to be a forged document.

66.8.b.1F

Paragraph (1E)(a) does not apply where—

66.8.b.1F.a

a discrepancy between the name of the holder of a specified document and the
name of the voter or proxy that the voter or proxy claims to be is resolved to
the presiding officer’s satisfaction at the time of the application by the
voter or proxy producing further proof of identity, and

66.8.b.1F.b

the presiding officer has no other reason (arising from any document produced
by the voter or proxy) to doubt that the voter or proxy is the voter or proxy
that the voter or proxy claims to be.

66.8.b.1G

The refusal to deliver a ballot paper to a voter or proxy under paragraph (1E)
does not prevent the voter or proxy making a further application under
paragraph (1), and paragraphs (1A) to (1F) apply on any further application.

66.8.b.1H

In this rule, a “ forged document ” means a false document made to resemble a
specified document.

66.8.b.1I

In this rule, a “specified document”—

66.8.b.1I.a

except in the case of a voter or proxy who has an anonymous entry in the
register of electors, is one which for the time being falls within the list
specified in rule 37(1H) of Schedule 1 to the 1983 Act (parliamentary election
rules);

66.8.b.1I.b

in the case of a voter or proxy who has an anonymous entry in the register of
electors, means an anonymous elector’s document which—

66.8.b.1I.b.i

was issued by the registration officer for the local authority in whose area
the referendum is held,

66.8.b.1I.b.ii

contains the number—

66.8.b.1I.b.ii.aa

allocated to the voter or proxy as stated in the copy of the register of
electors, or

66.8.b.1I.b.ii.bb

where an entry relating to the voter or proxy is added to the register in
pursuance of a notice issued under section 13B(3B) or (3D) of the 1983 Act, as
stated in the copy of that notice.

66.8.b.1J

Subject to paragraph (1K), a reference in this rule to a document that is a
specified document is a reference to the document regardless of any expiry
date relating to it.

66.8.b.1K

Paragraph (1J) does not apply to a temporary electoral identity document where
the date of the poll for the referendum is after the date for which the
document is issued.

66.8.b.1L

No person other than the presiding officer or a clerk may inspect a document
produced as proof of a voter’s identity, except as permitted by the voter.

66.8.b.1M

References in this rule to producing a document are to producing it for
inspection.

;

66.8.c

in paragraph (2), omit the words from “and only” to the end;

66.8.d

omit paragraph (3)(a).

66.9

In rule 28 (votes marked by the presiding officer)—

66.9.a

in paragraph (1), for “The” substitute  “Subject to paragraph (1A), the” ;

66.9.b

after paragraph (1) insert—

66.9.b.1A

Paragraphs (1A) to (1M) of rule 27 apply in the case of a voter or proxy who
applies under paragraph (a) as they apply in the case of a voter or proxy who
applies under rule 27(1), but as if—

66.9.b.1A.a

references to delivering a ballot paper to a voter or proxy were to causing a
voter’s or proxy’s vote to be marked on a ballot paper, and

66.9.b.1A.b

in rule 27(1G), the reference to paragraph (1) of rule 27 were to paragraph
(1) of this rule.

.

66.10

In rule 29 (voting by persons with disabilities)—

66.10.a

in paragraph (2), for “If” substitute  “Subject to paragraph (2A), if” ;

66.10.b

after paragraph (2) insert—

66.10.b.2A

Paragraphs (1A) to (1M) of rule 27 apply in the case of a voter or proxy who
applies under paragraph (a) as they apply in the case of a voter or proxy who
applies under rule 27(1), but as if—

66.10.b.2A.a

references to delivering a ballot paper to a voter or proxy were to granting a
voter’s or proxy’s application, and

66.10.b.2A.b

in rule 27(1G), the reference to paragraph (1) of rule 27 were to paragraph
(1) of this rule.

.

66.11

In rule 30 (tendered ballot papers: circumstances where available), after
paragraph (6) insert—

66.11.7

Paragraphs (1A) to (1M) of rule 27 apply in the case of a person who seeks to
mark a tendered ballot paper under this rule as they apply in the case of a
voter or proxy who applies for a ballot paper under rule 27(1), but as if in
rule 27(1G), the reference to making a further application under paragraph (1)
of rule 27 were to seeking a further time to mark a tendered ballot paper
under the paragraph of this rule under which a previous such attempt was made.

.

66.12

After rule 31 (tendered ballot papers: general provisions) insert—

########## Refusal to deliver ballot paper

66.12.31A

66.12.31A.1

Where a presiding officer refuses to deliver a ballot paper to a voter who
applied for one other than as a proxy, the officer or a clerk must enter on
the ballot paper refusal list—

66.12.31A.1.a

the voter’s electoral number, and

66.12.31A.1.b

against that number, the reason for the refusal.

66.12.31A.2

Where a presiding officer refuses to deliver a ballot paper to a voter who
applied for one as a proxy, the officer or a clerk must enter on the ballot
paper refusal list—

66.12.31A.2.a

the name and address of the voter, and

66.12.31A.2.b

against those details, the reason for the refusal.

66.12.31A.3

Paragraphs (4) and (5) apply where—

66.12.31A.3.a

a presiding officer refuses to deliver a ballot paper to a voter or proxy
under rule 27(1E), and

66.12.31A.3.b

the voter or proxy makes a further application under rule 27(1).

66.12.31A.4

If a ballot paper is delivered to the voter or proxy following a further
application, the presiding officer or a clerk must note that fact on the
ballot paper refusal list.

66.12.31A.5

If the presiding officer again refuses to deliver a ballot paper to the voter
or proxy, the presiding officer or a clerk must note that fact on the ballot
paper refusal list.

66.12.31A.6

Entries required by this rule to be made on the ballot paper refusal list must
be made as soon as practicable after delivery of a ballot paper to a voter or
proxy is refused (or, in the case mentioned in paragraph (4), as soon as
practicable after the delivery of a ballot paper to a voter or proxy).

66.12.31A.7

For the purposes of paragraph (1)(a), a person’s “electoral number” is the
number—

66.12.31A.7.a

allocated to the person as stated in the copy of the register of electors, or

66.12.31A.7.b

where an entry relating to the person is added to the register in pursuance of
a notice issued under section 13B(3B) or (3D) of the 1983 Act, as stated in
the copy of that notice.

66.12.31A.8

Subject to rule 27(1G) and paragraph (9), a refusal to deliver a ballot paper
to a voter or proxy is final and may not be questioned in any proceeding
whatsoever.

66.12.31A.9

A refusal to deliver a ballot paper to a voter or proxy is subject to review
in proceedings brought as mentioned in section 61N(3) of the 1990 Act.

66.12.31A.10

In this rule—

66.12.31A.10.a

except in paragraph (3)(a), any reference to the refusal to deliver a ballot
paper (however expressed) is to the refusal to do so under rule 25(3) or
27(1E), and

66.12.31A.10.b

any reference to paragraph (1E) or (1G) of rule 27 includes a reference to
that paragraph as applied by rule 28, 29 or 30.

.

the ballot paper refusal list completed in accordance with rule 31A;

66.14

66.15

In rule 45 (delivery of documents to relevant registration officer), in

the packet containing the completed ballot paper refusal list;

.

An order—

66.16.1A.a

for the opening of the sealed packet containing a completed ballot paper
refusal list, or

66.16.1A.b

for the inspection or production of that list,

may be made by the High Court or the county court if satisfied by evidence on
oath that the order is required for the purpose of proceedings brought as
mentioned in section 61N(3) of the 1990 Act.

.

#### Amendment of regulation 25 (questions to be put to persons signing the petition)

75

75.a

in the table following paragraph (1), in the column headed “Questions”, in

75.a.za

At a petition held in England, Wales or Scotland, “What is your name?”

75.a.zb

At a petition held in England, Wales or Scotland, “What is your address?”

;

after paragraph (3) insert—

75.b.3A

Where at a petition held in England, Wales or Scotland an assistant appointed
to assist the petition clerk—

75.b.3A.a

gives a person the required information (see paragraph (6)),

75.b.3A.b

puts a question specified in paragraph (1) to a person, and

75.b.3A.c

decides that the person has failed to answer the question satisfactorily,

the assistant must refer the matter to the petition clerk, who must put the
question to the person again.

;

75.c

in paragraph (4), for “A” substitute  “At a petition held in Northern Ireland,
a” ;

75.d

after paragraph (4) insert—

75.d.4A

Where at a petition held in England, Wales or Scotland the petition clerk—

75.d.4A.a

gives a person the required information,

75.d.4A.b

puts a question specified in paragraph (1) to the person (whether or not
following a referral under paragraph (3A)), and

75.d.4A.c

decides that the person has failed to answer the question satisfactorily,

the petition clerk must refuse to deliver a signing sheet to the person (and
see regulation 30A (procedure where signing sheet is refused under this
paragraph)).

75.d.4B

For the purposes of this regulation, a person answers the question “What is
your name?” or “What is your address?” satisfactorily if—

75.d.4B.a

where one of those questions is put, the answer matches a name or address (as
the case may be) in the register;

75.d.4B.b

where both those questions are put, the answers match a name and address in
that register that relate to the same person.

75.d.4C

In the case of an elector in respect of whom a notice has been issued under

(4B) are to be read as references to the notice issued under section 13BC(6).

;

petition)” ;

75.f

after paragraph (5) insert—

75.f.6

For the purposes of this regulation, a person to whom any question is to be
put is given “the required information” if the person is first informed that—

75.f.6.a

a signing sheet will be refused if the person fails to answer each question
satisfactorily, and

75.f.6.b

giving false information may be an offence.

.

#### Amendment of regulation 27 (signing procedure: England and Wales and Scotland)

76

76.1

Regulation 27 (signing procedure: England and Wales and Scotland) is amended
as follows.

76.2

In paragraph (1)—

76.2.a

for “A” substitute  “Subject to regulation 25(4A) and to paragraphs (1A) to
(1N), a” ;

76.2.b

omit sub-paragraph (a).

76.3

After paragraph (1) insert—

76.3.1A

A signing sheet must not be delivered to a person unless the person produces a
specified document to the petition clerk or an assistant to the petition
clerk.

76.3.1B

The petition clerk or assistant must arrange for the person to produce any
document in a private area of the petition signing place if the person so
requests, and, in such a case, must ensure that no other persons witness the
production except as permitted by the person.

76.3.1C

Paragraph (1D) applies in relation to a person where—

76.3.1C.a

the person produces a specified document to an assistant to the petition clerk
and the assistant decides that the document raises a reasonable doubt as to
whether the person is the elector or proxy that the person claims to be, or

76.3.1C.b

the person produces a document to an assistant that the assistant reasonably
suspects to be a forged document.

76.3.1D

Where this paragraph applies, the assistant must refer the matter and produce
the document to the petition clerk, who must proceed as if the person had
produced the document to the petition clerk in the first place.

76.3.1E

The petition clerk must refuse to deliver a signing sheet to a person where—

76.3.1E.a

the person produces a specified document to the clerk and the clerk decides
that the document raises a reasonable doubt as to whether the person is the
elector or proxy that the person claims to be, or

76.3.1E.b

the person produces a document to the clerk that the clerk reasonably suspects
to be a forged document.

76.3.1F

Paragraph (1E)(a) does not apply where—

76.3.1F.a

a discrepancy between the name of the holder of a specified document and the
name of the elector or proxy that the person claims to be is resolved to the
petition clerk’s satisfaction at the time of the application by the person
producing further proof of identity, and

76.3.1F.b

the petition clerk has no other reason (arising from any document produced by
the person) to doubt that the person is the elector or proxy that the person
claims to be.

76.3.1G

The refusal to deliver a signing sheet to a person under paragraph (1E) does
not prevent the voter making a further application under paragraph (1), and
paragraphs (1A) to (1F) apply on any further application.

76.3.1H

In this rule, a “ forged document ” means a false document made to resemble a
specified document.

76.3.1I

In this rule, a “specified document”—

76.3.1I.a

except in the case of a person who has an anonymous entry in the register, is
one which for the time being falls within the list specified in rule 37(1H) of
Schedule 1 to the 1983 Act (parliamentary election rules);

76.3.1I.b

in the case of a person who has an anonymous entry in the register, means an
anonymous elector’s document which—

76.3.1I.b.i

was issued by the appropriate registration officer;

76.3.1I.b.ii

contains the number allocated to the person as stated in the copy of the
register.

76.3.1J

(1J) In paragraph (1I)(b)(i), the “ appropriate registration officer ” means—

76.3.1J.a

the registration officer of the local authority in whose area the constituency
of the MP to whom the petition relates is situated, or

76.3.1J.b

where the petition relates to a constituency for which there is more than one
registration officer, any of those officers.

76.3.1K

Subject to paragraph (1L), a reference in this rule to a document that is a
specified document is a reference to the document regardless of any expiry
date relating to it.

76.3.1L

Paragraph (1K) does not apply to a temporary electoral identity document where
the date for which the temporary electoral identity document is issued is
before the designated day.

76.3.1M

No person other than the petition clerk or an assistant to the petition clerk
may inspect a document produced as proof of a person’s identity, except as
permitted by the person.

76.3.1N

References in this regulation to producing a document are to producing it for
inspection.

.

76.4

In paragraph (2), omit the words from “and only” to the end.

76.5

In paragraph (3), for “subparagraphs (a) and (c) of paragraph (1)” substitute
“paragraphs (1)(c) and (1I)(b)(ii)” .

#### New regulation 30A (refusal to deliver signing sheet: England and Wales and Scotland)

79

After regulation 30 (tendered signing sheets) insert—

######## Refusal to deliver signing sheet: England and Wales and Scotland

79.30A

79.30A.1

This regulation applies where a petition clerk refuses to deliver a signing
sheet under regulation 27(1E) (including that paragraph as applied by
regulation 29 (signing sheets endorsed by the petition clerk) or regulation 30
(tendered signing sheets)).

79.30A.2

Where a petition clerk refuses to deliver a signing sheet to a person who
applied for one as an elector, the clerk or an assistant to the clerk must
enter on the signing sheet refusal list—

79.30A.2.a

the person’s electoral number, and

79.30A.2.b

against that number, the reason for the refusal.

79.30A.3

Where a petition clerk refuses to deliver a signing sheet to a person who
applied for one as a proxy, the clerk or an assistant to the clerk must enter
on the signing sheet refusal list—

79.30A.3.a

the name and address of the elector, and

79.30A.3.b

against those details, the reason for the refusal.

79.30A.4

Paragraphs (5) and (6) apply where—

79.30A.4.a

a petition clerk refuses to deliver a signing sheet to a person under
regulation 27(1E), and

79.30A.4.b

the person makes a further application under regulation 27(1).

79.30A.5

If a signing sheet is delivered to the person following a further application,
the petition clerk or an assistant to the petition clerk must note that fact
on the signing sheet refusal list.

79.30A.6

If the petition clerk again refuses to deliver a signing sheet to the person,
the petition clerk or an assistant to the petition clerk must note that fact
on the signing sheet refusal list.

79.30A.7

Entries required by this regulation to be made to the signing sheet refusal
list must be made as soon as practicable after delivery of a signing sheet to
a person is refused (or, in the case mentioned in paragraph (5), as soon as
practicable after the delivery of a signing sheet to a person).

79.30A.8

For the purposes of paragraph (2)(a), a person’s “electoral number” is the
number—

79.30A.8.a

allocated to the person as stated in the copy of the register, or

79.30A.8.b

where an entry relating to the person is added to the register in pursuance of
a notice issued under section 13BC(6) of the 1983 Act, as stated in the copy
of that notice.

79.30A.9

Subject to regulation 27(1G) and paragraph (10), a refusal to deliver a
signing sheet to a person is final and may not be questioned in any proceeding
whatsoever.

79.30A.10

recall petition complaint.

or 27(1G), and

79.30A.11.b

any reference to paragraph (1E) or (1G) or regulation 27 includes a reference
to that paragraph as applied by regulation 29 or 30.

#### New regulation 71A (grounds relating to identification: England and Wales and Scotland)

90

After regulation 71 insert—

######## Grounds relating to identification: England and Wales and Scotland

90.71A

90.71A.1

For the purposes of this Part, an application is made on grounds relating to
identification if it is made because the following apply to B—

90.71A.1.a

condition 1, 2 or 3, and

90.71A.1.b

except where B has an anonymous entry in the register, condition 4.

90.71A.2

In this regulation, “ B ” means—

90.71A.2.a

the applicant, where—

90.71A.2.a.i

the application is made under regulation 53(2), and

90.71A.2.a.ii

regulation 63A(2) does not apply to the application made under regulation
57(7) which is included in that application under regulation 53(2);

90.71A.2.b

otherwise, the person already appointed as the applicant’s proxy at the time
the application is made.

90.71A.3

Condition 1 is that—

90.71A.3.a

immediately before the deadline, B has a specified document which B intends to
use to sign the petition in person, and

90.71A.3.b

after that deadline, that document is—

90.71A.3.b.i

lost, stolen, destroyed or damaged so as to be no longer usable as a specified
document for the purposes of that petition, or

90.71A.3.b.ii

sent by B to another person to prove B’s identity, and B considers it is
unlikely to be returned to B on or before the last day of the signing period
at that petition.

90.71A.4

Condition 2 is that—

90.71A.4.a

at a time during the period of 3 months ending with the deadline, B has
applied for a specified document,

90.71A.4.b

immediately before the deadline, B has not received that document, and

90.71A.4.c

the application for the specified document has not been refused or withdrawn.

90.71A.5

Condition 3 is that—

90.71A.5.a

B has an anonymous entry in the register, and

90.71A.5.b

either—

90.71A.5.b.i

B has not been issued with an anonymous elector’s document, or

90.71A.5.b.ii

B has been issued with an anonymous elector’s document, and after the deadline
B is allocated an electoral number which is different from the one shown on
that document other than as a result of an application under section 9B of the
1983 Act (anonymous registration).

90.71A.6

Condition 4 is that B does not have access to another specified document.

90.71A.7

In this regulation—

90.71A.7.a

the “ deadline ” means 5pm on the sixth day before the last day of the signing
period at the petition to which the application relates;

90.71A.7.b

“ specified document ” has the meaning given in regulation 27(1I).

.

94.8

In rule 37 (voting procedure)—

;

omit sub-paragraph (a);

94.8.b

after paragraph (1) insert—

94.8.b.1A

A ballot paper must not be delivered to a voter unless the voter produces a
specified document to the presiding officer or a clerk.

94.8.b.1B

The presiding officer or clerk must arrange for the voter to produce any
document in a private area of the polling station if the voter so requests,
and, in such a case, must ensure that no other persons witness the production
except as permitted by the voter.

94.8.b.1C

Paragraph (1D) applies in relation to a voter where—

94.8.b.1C.a

the voter produces a specified document to a clerk and the clerk decides that
the document raises a reasonable doubt as to whether the voter is the elector
or proxy that the voter claims to be, or

94.8.b.1C.b

the voter produces a document to a clerk that the clerk reasonably suspects to
be a forged document.

94.8.b.1D

Where this paragraph applies, the clerk must refer the matter and produce the
document to the presiding officer, who must proceed as if the voter had
produced the document to the presiding officer in the first place.

94.8.b.1E

The presiding officer must refuse to deliver a ballot paper to a voter where—

94.8.b.1E.a

the voter produces a specified document to the officer and the officer decides
that the document raises a reasonable doubt as to whether the voter is the
elector or proxy that the voter claims to be, or

94.8.b.1E.b

the voter produces a document to the officer that the officer reasonably
suspects to be a forged document.

94.8.b.1F

Paragraph (1E)(a) does not apply where—

94.8.b.1F.a

a discrepancy between the name of the holder of a specified document and the
name of the elector or proxy that the voter claims to be is resolved to the
presiding officer’s satisfaction at the time of the application by the voter
producing further proof of identity, and

94.8.b.1F.b

the presiding officer has no other reason (arising from any document produced
by the voter) to doubt that the voter is the elector or proxy that the voter
claims to be.

94.8.b.1G

The refusal to deliver a ballot paper to a voter under paragraph (1E) does not
prevent the voter making a further application under paragraph (1), and
paragraphs (1A) to (1F) apply on any further application.

94.8.b.1H

In this rule, a “ forged document ” means a false document made to resemble a
specified document.

94.8.b.1I

In this rule, a “specified document”—

94.8.b.1I.a

except in the case of a voter who has an anonymous entry in the register of
electors, means a document which for the time being falls within the list
specified in rule 37(1H) of Schedule 1 to the 1983 Act (parliamentary election
rules);

94.8.b.1I.b

in the case of a voter who has an anonymous entry in the register of electors,
means an anonymous elector’s document which—

94.8.b.1I.b.i

was issued by the registration officer for the constituent council in whose
area the polling station to which the voter is allotted is situated,

94.8.b.1I.b.ii

contains the number—

94.8.b.1I.b.ii.aa

allocated to the voter as stated in the copy of the register of electors, or

94.8.b.1I.b.ii.bb

where an entry relating to the voter is added to the register in pursuance of
a notice issued under section 13B(3B) or (3D) of the 1983 Act, as stated in
the copy of that notice.

94.8.b.1J

Subject to paragraph (1K), a reference in this rule to a document that is a
specified document is a reference to the document regardless of any expiry
date relating to it.

94.8.b.1K

Paragraph (1J) does not apply to a temporary electoral identity document where
the date of the poll for the election is after the date for which the document
is issued.

94.8.b.1L

No person other than the presiding officer or a clerk may inspect a document
produced as proof of a voter’s identity, except as permitted by the voter.

94.8.b.1M

References in this rule to producing a document are to producing it for
inspection.

;

in paragraph (2), omit the words from “and only” to the end;

94.8.d

omit paragraph (3)(a).

94.12

After rule 41 (tendered ballot papers—general provisions) insert—

########## Refusal to deliver ballot paper

94.12.41A

94.12.41A.1

Where a presiding officer refuses to deliver a ballot paper to a voter who
applied for one as an elector, the officer or a clerk must enter on the ballot
paper refusal list—

94.12.41A.1.a

the voter’s electoral number, and

94.12.41A.1.b

against that number, the reason for the refusal.

94.12.41A.2

Where a presiding officer refuses to deliver a ballot paper to a voter who
applied for one as a proxy, the officer or a clerk must enter on the ballot
paper refusal list—

94.12.41A.2.a

the name and address of the voter, and

94.12.41A.2.b

against those details, the reason for the refusal.

94.12.41A.3

Paragraphs (4) and (5) apply where—

94.12.41A.3.a

a presiding officer refuses to deliver a ballot paper to a voter under rule
37(1E), and

94.12.41A.3.b

the voter makes a further application as permitted by rule 37(1G).

94.12.41A.4

If a ballot paper is delivered to the voter following that application, the
presiding officer or a clerk must note that fact on the ballot paper refusal
list.

94.12.41A.5

If the presiding officer again refuses to deliver a ballot paper to the voter,
the presiding officer or a clerk must note that fact on the ballot paper
refusal list.

94.12.41A.6

Entries required by this rule to be made on the ballot paper refusal list must
be made as soon as practicable after delivery of a ballot paper to a voter is
refused (or, in the case mentioned in paragraph (4), as soon as practicable
after the delivery of a ballot paper to a voter).

94.12.41A.7

For the purposes of paragraph (1)(a), a person’s “electoral number” is the
number—

94.12.41A.7.a

allocated to the person as stated in the copy of the register of electors, or

94.12.41A.7.b

where an entry relating to the person is added to the register in pursuance of
a notice issued under section 13B(3B) or (3D) of the 1983 Act, as stated in
the copy of that notice.

94.12.41A.8

Subject to rule 37(1G) and paragraph (9), a refusal to deliver a ballot paper
to a voter is final and may not be questioned in any proceeding whatsoever.

94.12.41A.9

A refusal to deliver a ballot paper to a voter is subject to review on an
election petition.

94.12.41A.10

In this rule—

94.12.41A.10.a

except in paragraph (3)(a), any reference to the refusal to deliver a ballot
paper (however expressed) is to the refusal to do so under rule 35(3) or
37(1E), and

94.12.41A.10.b

any reference to paragraph (1E) or (1G) of rule 37 includes a reference to
that paragraph as applied by rule 38, 39 or 40.

########## Collection and disclosure of information relating to applications made under rules 37 to 40

94.12.41B

94.12.41B.1

This rule applies in relation to an election to which the Secretary of State’s
duty under section 59A(4) of the 1983 Act (reports on voter identification
requirements in respect of local government elections) applies by virtue of
subsection (5A) of that section.

94.12.41B.2

The presiding officer must—

94.12.41B.2.a

collect the information described in regulation  34  of the Voter
Identification Regulations 2022 (collection of information by presiding
officer) relating to applications made under rules 37(1), 38(1), 39(1) or
40(1), and

94.12.41B.2.b

provide that information to the returning officer as soon as practicable after
the close of the poll.

94.12.41B.3

The returning officer must forward the information to the relevant
registration officer.

94.12.41B.4

As soon as reasonably practicable after receiving the information the relevant
registration officer must—

94.12.41B.4.a

anonymise the information by removing from it all names and electoral numbers
of the people to whom the information relates, and

94.12.41B.4.b

collate the information in accordance with regulation  35  of the Voter
Identification Regulations 2022 (collation of information by relevant
registration officer).

The information as anonymised and collated in accordance with this paragraph
is referred to in the rest of this rule as “the paragraph (4) information”.

94.12.41B.5

The relevant registration officer must provide the paragraph (4) information—

94.12.41B.5.a

to the Secretary of State, as soon as reasonably practicable after taking the
steps required by paragraph (4), and

94.12.41B.5.b

where they request the information, to the Electoral Commission.

94.12.41B.6

The relevant registration officer must not disclose the paragraph (4)
information otherwise than in accordance with paragraph (5).

94.12.41B.7

The relevant registration officer must retain the information anonymised in
accordance with paragraph (4)(a) for at least 10 years.

94.12.41B.8

For the purpose of paragraph (4)(a), a person’s “electoral number” is the
number—

94.12.41B.8.a

allocated to the person as stated in the copy of the register of electors, or

94.12.41B.8.b

where an entry relating to the person is added to the register in pursuance of
a notice issued under section 13B(3B) or (3D) of the 1983 Act, as stated in
the copy of that notice.

94.12.41B.9

Except as provided by paragraph (10), a disclosure of information under this
rule does not breach—

94.12.41B.9.a

any obligation of confidence owed by the presiding officer, the returning
officer or a registration officer, or

94.12.41B.9.b

any other restriction on the disclosure of information (however imposed).

94.12.41B.10

Nothing in this rule authorises the making of a disclosure that contravenes
the data protection legislation (but in determining whether a disclosure would
do so, the duties imposed by paragraphs (2) and (3) are to be taken into
account).

94.12.41B.11

In this rule—

94.12.41B.11.a

“ the data protection legislation ” has the same meaning as in the Data
Protection Act 2018;

94.12.41B.11.b

references to the relevant registration officer are to the registration
officer of the constituent council in relation to whose area the returning
officer exercises functions under this Order.

.

(d) insert—

94.13.da

the ballot paper refusal list completed in accordance with rule 41A,

.

94.14.ba

the completed ballot paper refusal list,

.

94.15.ca

the packet containing the completed ballot paper refusal list,

.

94.16.1A

94.16.1A.a

for the opening of the sealed packet containing a completed ballot paper
refusal list, or

94.16.1A.b

for the inspection or production of that list,

may be made by the county court if satisfied by evidence on oath that the
order is required for the purpose of an election petition.

What is your name?

96.8

In rule 37 (voting procedure)—

96.8.a

in paragraph (1)—

96.8.a.i

for “A” substitute  “Subject to rule 35(3) and to paragraphs (1A) to (1M), a”
;

96.8.a.ii

omit sub-paragraph (a);

96.8.b

after paragraph (1) insert—

96.8.b.1A

A ballot paper must not be delivered to a voter unless the voter produces a
specified document to the presiding officer or a clerk.

96.8.b.1B

The presiding officer or clerk must arrange for the voter to produce any
document in a private area of the polling station if the voter so requests,
and, in such a case, must ensure that no other persons witness the production
except as permitted by the voter.

96.8.b.1C

Paragraph (1D) applies in relation to a voter where—

96.8.b.1C.a

the voter produces a specified document to a clerk and the clerk decides that
the document raises a reasonable doubt as to whether the voter is the elector
or proxy that the voter claims to be, or

96.8.b.1C.b

the voter produces a document to a clerk that the clerk reasonably suspects to
be a forged document.

96.8.b.1D

Where this paragraph applies, the clerk must refer the matter and produce the
document to the presiding officer, who must proceed as if the voter had
produced the document to the presiding officer in the first place.

96.8.b.1E

The presiding officer must refuse to deliver a ballot paper to a voter where—

96.8.b.1E.a

the voter produces a specified document to the officer and the officer decides
that the document raises a reasonable doubt as to whether the voter is the
elector or proxy that the voter claims to be, or

96.8.b.1E.b

the voter produces a document to the officer that the officer reasonably
suspects to be a forged document.

96.8.b.1F

Paragraph (1E)(a) does not apply where—

96.8.b.1F.a

a discrepancy between the name of the holder of a specified document and the
name of the elector or proxy that the voter claims to be is resolved to the
presiding officer’s satisfaction at the time of the application by the voter
producing further proof of identity, and

96.8.b.1F.b

the presiding officer has no other reason (arising from any document produced
by the voter) to doubt that the voter is the elector or proxy that the voter
claims to be.

96.8.b.1G

The refusal to deliver a ballot paper to a voter under paragraph (1E) does not
prevent the voter making a further application under paragraph (1), and
paragraphs (1A) to (1F) apply on any further application.

96.8.b.1H

In this rule, a “ forged document ” means a false document made to resemble a
specified document.

96.8.b.1I

In this rule, a “specified document”—

96.8.b.1I.a

except in the case of a voter who has an anonymous entry in the register of
electors, means a document which for the time being falls within the list
specified in rule 37(1H) of Schedule 1 to the 1983 Act (parliamentary election
rules);

96.8.b.1I.b

in the case of a voter who has an anonymous entry in the register of electors,
means an anonymous elector’s document which—

96.8.b.1I.b.i

was issued by the registration officer for the constituent council in whose
area the polling station to which the voter is allotted is situated,

96.8.b.1I.b.ii

contains the number—

96.8.b.1I.b.ii.aa

allocated to the voter as stated in the copy of the register of electors, or

96.8.b.1I.b.ii.bb

where an entry relating to the voter is added to the register in pursuance of
a notice issued under section 13B(3B) or (3D) of the 1983 Act, as stated in
the copy of that notice.

96.8.b.1J

Subject to paragraph (1K), a reference in this rule to a document that is a
specified document is a reference to the document regardless of any expiry
date relating to it.

96.8.b.1K

Paragraph (1J) does not apply to a temporary electoral identity document where
the date of the poll for the election is after the date for which the document
is issued.

96.8.b.1L

No person other than the presiding officer or a clerk may inspect a document
produced as proof of a voter’s identity, except as permitted by the voter.

96.8.b.1M

References in this rule to producing a document are to producing it for
inspection.

;

96.8.c

in paragraph (2), omit the words from “and only” to the end;

96.8.d

omit paragraph (3)(a).

96.12

After rule 41 (tendered ballot papers—general provisions) insert—

########## Refusal to deliver ballot paper

96.12.41A

96.12.41A.1

Where a presiding officer refuses to deliver a ballot paper to a voter who
applied for one as an elector, the officer or a clerk must enter on the ballot
paper refusal list—

96.12.41A.1.a

the voter’s electoral number, and

96.12.41A.1.b

against that number, the reason for the refusal.

96.12.41A.2

Where a presiding officer refuses to deliver a ballot paper to a voter who
applied for one as a proxy, the officer or a clerk must enter on the ballot
paper refusal list—

96.12.41A.2.a

the name and address of the voter, and

96.12.41A.2.b

against those details, the reason for the refusal.

96.12.41A.3

Paragraphs (4) and (5) apply where—

96.12.41A.3.a

a presiding officer refuses to deliver a ballot paper to a voter under rule
37(1E), and

96.12.41A.3.b

the voter makes a further application as permitted by rule 37(1G).

96.12.41A.4

If a ballot paper is delivered to the voter following that application, the
presiding officer or a clerk must note that fact on the ballot paper refusal
list.

96.12.41A.5

If the presiding officer again refuses to deliver a ballot paper to the voter,
the presiding officer or a clerk must note that fact on the ballot paper
refusal list.

96.12.41A.6

Entries required by this rule to be made on the ballot paper refusal list must
be made as soon as practicable after delivery of a ballot paper to a voter is
refused (or, in the case mentioned in paragraph (4), as soon as practicable
after the delivery of a ballot paper to a voter).

96.12.41A.7

For the purposes of paragraph (1)(a), a person’s “electoral number” is the
number—

96.12.41A.7.a

allocated to the person as stated in the copy of the register of electors, or

96.12.41A.7.b

where an entry relating to the person is added to the register in pursuance of
a notice issued under section 13B(3B) or (3D) of the 1983 Act, as stated in
the copy of that notice.

96.12.41A.8

Subject to rule 37(1G) and paragraph (9), a refusal to deliver a ballot paper
to a voter is final and may not be questioned in any proceeding whatsoever.

96.12.41A.9

A refusal to deliver a ballot paper to a voter is subject to review on an
election petition.

96.12.41A.10

In this rule—

96.12.41A.10.a

except in paragraph (3)(a), any reference to the refusal to deliver a ballot
paper (however expressed) is to the refusal to do so under rule 35(3) or
37(1E), and

96.12.41A.10.b

any reference to paragraph (1E) or (1G) of rule 37 includes a reference to
that paragraph as applied by rule 38, 39 or 40.

########## Collection and disclosure of information relating to applications made under rules 37 to 40

96.12.41B

96.12.41B.1

This rule applies in relation to an election to which the Secretary of State’s
duty under section 59A(4) of the 1983 Act (reports on voter identification
requirements in respect of local government elections) applies by virtue of
subsection (5A) of that section.

96.12.41B.2

The presiding officer must—

96.12.41B.2.a

collect the information described in regulation  34  of the Voter
Identification Regulations 2022 (collection of information by presiding
officer) relating to applications made under rules 37(1), 38(1), 39(1) or
40(1), and

96.12.41B.2.b

provide that information to the returning officer as soon as practicable after
the close of the poll.

96.12.41B.3

The returning officer must forward the information to the relevant
registration officer.

96.12.41B.4

As soon as reasonably practicable after receiving the information the relevant
registration officer must—

96.12.41B.4.a

anonymise the information by removing from it all names and electoral numbers
of the people to whom the information relates, and

96.12.41B.4.b

collate the information in accordance with regulation  35  of the Voter
Identification Regulations 2022 (collation of information by relevant
registration officer).

The information as anonymised and collated in accordance with this paragraph
is referred to in the rest of this rule as “the paragraph (4) information”.

96.12.41B.5

The relevant registration officer must provide the paragraph (4) information—

96.12.41B.5.a

to the Secretary of State, as soon as reasonably practicable after taking the
steps required by paragraph (4), and

96.12.41B.5.b

where they request the information, to the Electoral Commission.

96.12.41B.6

The relevant registration officer must not disclose the paragraph (4)
information otherwise than in accordance with paragraph (5).

96.12.41B.7

The relevant registration officer must retain the information anonymised in
accordance with paragraph (4)(a) for at least 10 years.

96.12.41B.8

For the purpose of paragraph (4)(a), a person’s “electoral number” is the
number—

96.12.41B.8.a

allocated to the person as stated in the copy of the register of electors, or

96.12.41B.8.b

where an entry relating to the person is added to the register in pursuance of
a notice issued under section 13B(3B) or (3D) of the 1983 Act, as stated in
the copy of that notice.

96.12.41B.9

Except as provided by paragraph (10), a disclosure of information under this
rule does not breach—

96.12.41B.9.a

any obligation of confidence owed by the presiding officer, the returning
officer or a registration officer, or

96.12.41B.9.b

any other restriction on the disclosure of information (however imposed).

96.12.41B.10

Nothing in this rule authorises the making of a disclosure that contravenes
the data protection legislation (but in determining whether a disclosure would
do so, the duties imposed by paragraphs (2) and (3) are to be taken into
account).

96.12.41B.11

In this rule—

96.12.41B.11.a

“ the data protection legislation ” has the same meaning as in the Data
Protection Act 2018;

96.12.41B.11.b

references to the relevant registration officer are to the registration
officer of the constituent council in relation to whose area the returning
officer exercises functions under this Order.

.

96.13

In rule 45 (procedure on close of poll), in paragraph (1) after sub-paragraph
(d) insert—

96.13.da

the ballot paper refusal list completed in accordance with rule 41A,

.

96.14

In rule 61 (sealing up of ballot papers), in paragraph (2) after sub-paragraph
(b) insert—

96.14.ba

the completed ballot paper refusal list,

.

96.15

In rule 62 (delivery and retention of documents), after paragraph (c) insert—

96.15.ca

the packet containing the completed ballot paper refusal list,

.

96.16

In rule 63 (orders for production of documents), after paragraph (1) insert—

96.16.1A

An order—

96.16.1A.a

for the opening of the sealed packet containing a completed ballot paper
refusal list, or

96.16.1A.b

for the inspection or production of that list,

may be made by the county court if satisfied by evidence on oath that the
order is required for the purpose of an election petition.

.

96.17

In Part 9 (appendix of forms)—

96.17.a

in the list of forms, after the entry “Form 11: Official proxy postal poll
card” insert  “Form 11A: Ballot paper refusal list” ;

96.17.b

for Form 8 (official poll card) substitute the corresponding form in Part 2 of
Schedule 13;

96.17.c

for Form 10 (official proxy poll card) substitute the corresponding form in
Part 2 of Schedule 13;

96.17.d

after Form 11 (official proxy postal poll card) insert new Form 11A (ballot
paper refusal list) as set out in Part 2 of Schedule 13;

96.17.e

for Form 12 (directions for the guidance of voters) substitute the
corresponding form in Part 2 of Schedule 13.
